when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她確實做了一些 , 但實際上 , 真正的一件事是說 , 未來會更加遠大於這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 他又發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴貝奇的機器是純機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是理論性的
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但turing告訴我們一些很重要的事情 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你怎麼做電腦都無所謂 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	你的電腦是不是像babbage那樣是純機械的 , 或者像現在的電腦是電子的 , 或者是未來的電腦 , 或者是細胞 , 或者再一次的 , 又或者 , 再說一次 , 機械性的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米技術 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得很小 。 這些都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂巡迴論文 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你開始連結了 , 你說巴貝奇做的東西真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它可以做到現在我們用電腦可以做到的所有事情 , 只是真的很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道它有多慢 , 它有大約1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	並且使用打孔卡 , 也就是被餵食的 , 打孔卡的速度比第一輛zx81快一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它確實有一群ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想的話 , 你可以添加很多額外的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 這又帶我們到哪裡去 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有一些計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的文章由charlesbabbage撰寫 , 內容是關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一系列計畫被我們稱為計畫28 , 這同時也是我和doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字 , doronswade是科學博物館中管理電腦的成員 , 也是起草了這個計劃要建造出一個不一樣引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是把它做出來 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南區 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一項就是掃描babbage的文獻
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這是已經完成的 。 第二個是關於這些計劃的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬那台機器的電腦 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館裡進行的 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	一旦完成 , 你就會明白電腦是如何運作 , 因為你面前有一小塊晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 我聞到它的味道 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要進行模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫到:一旦分析引擎真的存在 , 它一定會引導未來的科學步驟 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有把它做出來 , 因為他總是在小試新計劃 , 但當它真的在1940年代被做出來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我讓你們稍微聽一下它的動作是什麼樣子 , 影片中只展示出cpu機械的運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪它將會加上 。 這是加法的運作所以 , 想像一下這台巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代之前 , 我們會有 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在充滿形象的演說中 , 雅南•亞特伯特蘭展示了他三項關於人性的近期計畫 , 我們的棲息地在他的 「 地圖上 」 當中 , 他的作品在世界各地的個人訪問 , 標出了他的 「 六十億其它人 」 , 以及他剛出版的電影 , 「 家庭 」 , 這部紀錄了人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影技術 ,
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅納•阿特伯特用廣角的角度捕捉世界很脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以乘飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了9噸二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態學 , 第一年 , 我以法國人的二氧化碳排放量來排放量 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來減碳 , 像我每次都做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是向大家展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 關於我去年拍攝的最後一幅照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的油砂 , 很多的污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題所在 ; 我們不想相信已知的事物 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們每天工作24小時 , 每七小時一班去採石油 , 盡可能抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油終結
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油砂不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量卻是三倍之多 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信已知的事實 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚因全球暖化而被消滅 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 且對海洋的多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極是我在去年夏天拍的照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	十五年前 , 做這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在有一條新途徑 , 在大西洋和太平洋之間 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	自1960年起 , 北極的厚度就下降了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	沒有冰的吉力馬扎羅的新面孔
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	據科學家估計 , 在一百年內 , 所有高山的冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	正如艾爾•高爾所說 , 20億人住在水上 , 住在喜馬拉雅山的冰河上 。
return of fish men .	漁夫回來了 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一人類是依靠魚而活 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今有70%的魚庫被過度開發 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據聯合國的資料 , 如果我們不改變捕魚系統的主要資源 , 2050年就會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信已知的事實 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	這張美麗的照片 , 由[不清楚]在非洲 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	世界上有六個人沒有足夠的食物 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人沒有足夠的食物 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米在許多地方是其中之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 耕種的90%的玉米被用來餵養動物或石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅洲棕櫚樹種植園 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每一年 , 我們在森林中就損失了五萬平方英哩的面積 。

i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。

12th man: if i was to go back to iraq and speak to the people , i'd have to bow down and kiss their feet .	第十二個男人:如果我回到伊拉克 , 向人民說話 , 我就得要放下腳 , 親吻他們的腳 。
just as that woman tried to kiss my feet when we were taking her sons .	就如同那位女子在我們接觸她的兒子時試圖親吻我的腳 。
and i feel humbled by their strength .	我因為他們的力量而感到謙卑 。
and i will forever feel a need to make reparations to iraq .	我永遠會覺得有必要向伊拉克做點名 。

at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	在那一刻 , 我的家人很窮 , 我在深圳的生活 , 就是要展現自己 , 我可以賺更多 , 讓父母去過生活 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經四十五億歲了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物已有數億年歷史 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類也直立行走僅20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們成功地適應 , 並且征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世世代以來 , 我們養育我們的孩子 , 和我們身邊的其他數百萬物種沒什麼不同 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年 , 我從高空中觀察地球和它的居民 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活依賴於地球的福祉 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕撈、繁殖、農耕至今仍是人類最重要的工作 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	將我們連結在一起的程度 , 遠大於分化我們的力量 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們對地球的禮物都有同樣的需求 , 希望能超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而我們卻繼續在牆壁上築牆 , 來讓我們保持距離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天我們最大的挑戰是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們已經徹底改變了它 , 遠超過了人類歷史的全部 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的運輸很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	集約農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 ,
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但 , 財富落差越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒有意識到我們正以比這星球能承受的更快的速度前進 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道 , 現今就有解決方案 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 , 變得更好 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們還在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講裡 , 理查德•雷斯尼克揭示出 , 原本便宜又快速的基因測序將如何顛覆健康照護 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療保健、科學、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德.雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因體革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我為你們介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性別染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男人有x , 當然還有那個y的小複本 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	很抱歉 , 男士們 , 但這只是讓你與眾不同的小東西 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 會發現 , 雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼是由四個生物化學字母所組成 , 我們稱之為基對:a、c、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少基因 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	每個人都可以隨便亂丟大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但如果我把這1280年像素點一個基對 , 像素在800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 有一群人有y染色體 , 最後決定想定序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以15年後 , 大約40億美金後 , 基因組定序和發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最終的版本被出版了 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個基底都要花1塊美金 , 非常慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我在這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以我們做的是將一個基因組複製50份然後把所有的複製品切成50基對然後我們對它們進行大量平行排序
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它放入軟體中 , 重新組合起來 , 告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看看這看起來是什麼樣子 , 人類基因組計劃:3gabas , 對吧 ?
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器跑來跑一台:每週2000億基對 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變到600年 , 這個速度完全沒有減速的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以基礎定序的價格已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這就相當於你在1998年便把車裝滿氣體 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開著木星和木星回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc位置、所有醫學文獻的存檔、摩爾定律、古老的排序法 , 所有的新東西都是如此 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數尺度的圖 , 你通常不會看到這些線條向上移動 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界對於人類基因組的測序能力 , 今年約有5萬到10萬人 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們從已被放置的機器中知道這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期未來會加倍、三倍 , 或四倍 , 年復一年 , 才會有可預見的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室 , 代表著所有這些能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做 " 北京基因研究所 " 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人在贏得這場新月球的比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以女人37歲了 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她的乳癌會出現在第2個雌激素受體處的乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受了手術 , 化療以及放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她又發現了三期的卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用的是手術和化療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她42歲回來 , 卵巢癌愈多 , 化療愈多 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又患上了急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	八天後 , 她陷入呼吸衰竭 ,
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	所以 , 首先 , 在短短的10年中 , 這個女人被對待的方式 , 看起來就像在做血液檢查 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	正因為像我在華盛頓大學基因研究所的同事rickwilson決定要研究這位女士 ,
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他進行了基因測序 , 取了皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚、和癌細胞的骨髓 , 他將兩者的基因組排列做了幾週 , 沒什麼大不了的基因組 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他在軟體中比較這兩組基因 , 他發現 , 在其他方面 , 一個叫做tp53的基因缺損 , 在三十億個鹼基中 , 出現了一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你有這種基因遺傳突變 , 你一生中就有90%會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位婦女沒有任何幫助 , 但如果你願意 , 這對她的家人卻有很大的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 且他們有基因測試 , 且他們能了解 , 那他們就能定期做篩檢 , 能及早發現癌症 , 很有可能可以過更長的人生 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我為各位介紹beery雙胞胎 , 診斷出2歲的腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女士 , 她不相信這些症狀與眾不同 , 透過一些英雄的努力和網路搜尋 , 她說服了醫療團體 , 其實他們還有別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們的肌肉動脈不正常 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了左旋多巴 , 而他們的症狀確實有改善 , 但他們沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片裡的這位先生叫做joebeery , 他很幸運能擔任一家叫做生命科技的公司的執行長 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家製造大量基因定序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他做的是把他的孩子定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現在一個叫做spr的基因中有一系列突變 , 負責產生血清素和其他物質 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左旋多巴的基礎上 , 他們給了這些孩子使用血清素的前身藥物 , 現在他們是正常的 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有全部的基因定序 , 這種事永遠不會發生 。

so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	喜歡蝙蝠俠和水槍 。

and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是他在吃東西的時候 , 而是當他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸道會打開排泄物外流進他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	經過一百次手術 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請求我 , 我好痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們把這孩子的基因定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現的是在一個控制細胞死亡的基因上 , 一個控制基因上有單點變異 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以這個理論是 , 他對本質上發生的事情 , 產生了一種對食物的免疫反應 , 而這是一種自然反應 , 導致了一些被編譯過的細胞死亡 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫婦的骨髓移除一套新的設備 , 很快收集骨髓的最小痛楚 。 他強調骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞可以被用來治療許多絕症狀 , 從帕金森症到心臟疾病 。

so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收成這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 和我的另一位醫師 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃在桌上 , 我們拿了一根小針 , 你知道的 , 不夠大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們將它放入軟組織 , 將它浸入硬骨 , 進入tuchus , 每一次用針筒吸出大約十毫升的骨髓 ,
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後將牠交給護士 , 牠將牠注射到一塊錫上 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把針筒交給我 , 一而再、再而三地傳給我 。
about 200 times usually .	大約二百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我的手臂末端是索雷爾 , 我手上有通話機 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個手術在40年以來沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	應該有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想出了一個微不足道的新裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而這個採礦者 , 它的運作方式在這裡 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準 「 看 」 病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	我們不但沒有進入骨頭數十次 , 而是直接進入髖骨前或臀部後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性的導管有一個特殊的電線圈尖端 , 它留在骨髓內的殘酷部位 , 隨着臀部的輪廓移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	它能讓你快速地渴望 , 或快速地吸乾富骨髓 , 迅速穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過相同的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , bob只需要一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 並以病人的身分收穫 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 我在史丹佛拿到一些小額資助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	稍微玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們拿了兩個大型動物和豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	令人驚訝的是 , 我們不但沒有得到骨髓 , 還從骨髓採取的幹細胞活動 , 比普通裝置的骨髓多出十倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個設備在去年才剛通過食品及藥物管理局批准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是一個活體病患 , 你可以看到它跟著一個柔軟的曲線移動 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 有兩次路程來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	以局部麻醉為例 , 以門診為例 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	而我們從同一個病人身上得到三至六倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 為什麼你要在乎 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞遍佈我們的身體 , 包括我們骨髓中血液循環的幹細胞 , 我們已經用它作為幹細胞治療的一種形式 , 長達40年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 利用骨髓幹細胞治療病人的其他疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、心臟病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經學上治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	今年 , 我們剛剛公佈 , 我們正在推行2.0的 「 骨髓採取器 」 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能取出更多幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你去銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年輕和健康時 , 去使用未來你需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後這是一張我們骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 他們每年都會到史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來能有更多這樣的存活者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者高斯提出了對宇宙的有爭議的新模型 , 答案可能是所有大問題的答案 。 如果沒別的 , 那就是基本粒子和力量的八度模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	葛雷特利西的萬物理論是關於他對萬物的理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	喔 , 老兄 。 看看這些殺手級的方程式 。 甜點 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我將盡我所能描述粒子物理的美好 , 不用算式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗又特別的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚都有成千上萬的珊瑚樣本 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會不斷地繁殖和分裂 , 變成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這珊瑚是超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以找個人 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 相較於他的鄰居 , 他究竟是如何變成這樣 ? 如果只是巧合 , 或是命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們收到足以把溫度提高之後 , 他就會告訴我們 , 我們的問題很愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚有很大的意義 , 我有衝浪式的疤痕可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	這珊瑚還會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居和他一模一樣 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在所有其他地點都一樣 , 但也體驗到他們是不同的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分支成不同的珊瑚是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是超級聰明的珊瑚已準備好理解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學方法非常準確地描述了宇宙的運行方式 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們現實世界和珊瑚一樣 , 不斷有不同的可能性 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是很奇怪的 , 把我們的頭腦包住 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的奇特現象最早是由薛丁格和他的貓提出來的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設置中 , 薛丁格在一個具放射性的樣本的箱子中 , 根據量子力學的定律 , 要將他放射線擴展到一個狀態 , 而這個狀態不是放射線性的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在輻射劑的枝幹中 , 它觸發的部分會釋放毒藥 , 而薛丁格已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支裡 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都會經歷到這些實相 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	不管怎麼說 , 另一個不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只能獨立存在 , 而且我們還無法看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每個人 , 像薛丁格 , 都有點像是珊瑚分化成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都會發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示所有事情都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理學的其他部分則是要描述什麼會發生 , 什麼不會 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都歸功於幾何以及基本粒子的交互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	唯有這些互動是完全平衡的才能實現 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我將描述一下我們對這些粒子的了解它們是什麼以及它們的平衡是如何運作的
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這部機器中質子和反質子被加速到接近光速的速度然後相撞產生出一股巨大的純能量
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴灑 , 裝上偵測器和電腦 , 用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個在日內瓦cern的大型強子對撞機周長有17英里 , 當它在運作時 , 所產生的能量相當於蒙特雷市的5倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確地預測哪些粒子會在每一次撞擊中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們一切皆可能
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們哪些粒子會被製造出來 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質子和能量都必須有相同的質子和反質子
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何的粒子都比這個能量極限更大 , 都不會產生 , 且保持我們看不見 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這也是為什麼粒子加速器如此振奮人心的原因 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	能量的極限會是以前所未有的七倍 , 所以我們很快就會看到新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 先讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子的粒子有很多動物園 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	大部分人都很熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這個房間裡的很多人過著良好的生活
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子有個中性夥伴 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷 , 和很小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上夸克有較大的質量 , 三者結合之後 , 就能在原子裡製造光子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	這些粒子分為左旋和右旋它們都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代電量和第一代相同但質量更高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子會和各種力量產生交互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子傳送電荷相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	另外還有一個非常微不足道的力 , 非常不可思議的弱力 , 只有和左旋物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力動力 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 稱為顏色載荷 , 由三種不同的紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以責怪murraygellmann , 因為這些名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後是重力 , 通過物體的質量和旋轉的作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都對應有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力通過各自粒子所攜帶的載荷相互作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在的存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它能給所有其他的粒子質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎可以確定會如此 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的奧秘在於我們還能看到什麼 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要給你們看一個美麗的可能性 , 給你們看這次演講的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷計算所有這些不同的粒子總共有226種
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多能被追蹤的粒子 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子是很奇怪的 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們依據他們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 一些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷而夸克在三分之一就有電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子 , 它有一個正電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 一種相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這個模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做電弱統一模型 , 它於1967年被組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以對電荷非常熟悉卻不是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量打破了電弱排列的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它的弱力之所以弱 , 是因為它給予弱粒子較大的質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯粒子在水準方向分佈電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量而且在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力是用這種二度空間的粒子載荷模式來描述的 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來 , 將載荷用夸克形式沿這些方向畫出來 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度空間中畫出來然後投影到二度空間以便我們能看到這些粒子
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 大自然就會在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞會產生能量四個載荷方向都是零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 只要能量相同和載荷總量為零就能產生任何物質 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可能會在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱粒子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個粒子仍然可以做到零電荷
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不只漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們 , 什麼樣的互動是被允許的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間可以更好地觀察強相互作用 , 有很好的六角形的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	強相互作用時 , 強力粒子 , 比如這個 , 會和有色夸克互動 , 比如這個綠色的 , 給夸克一個紅色的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每個原子中發生數百萬次 , 將原子核固定在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但和三種力相對應的這四種載荷還不是故事的終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以把引力相對應的兩個載荷放進去 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們納入時 , 每個粒子的旋轉載荷有兩個不同的旋轉載荷、旋轉和旋轉載荷 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中呈現一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看上去很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種圖形符合我們目前對於大自然的最佳知識 , 與這些基本粒子的微小世界相對應 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們很確定的事 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗中非常受限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙運作的方式是如此地美麗 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但我現在要來談一些關於我們還不知道的新舊觀念 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要只用數學方法來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能否把我們的手放到全芝加拿大 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到構成宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們希望用這張圖來預測新的粒子 , 何時試驗到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個舊的想法 , 就是這種不對稱的載荷圖案 , 從一個比較完美的圖案中產生 , 和希格斯粒子破壞電弱的圖案很類似 , 導致電磁性產生 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了達成這個目的 , 我們需要引入新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引導一個新的方向時 , 我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子的載荷 , 然後我們就可以讓它跟其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果猜對的話 , 我們可以在六度載荷空間中建構標準載荷 , 做為一個破壞的對稱 , 來達到最完美的七度載荷空間 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 帕蒂和沙拉姆提出了這項特殊的統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的統一圖案 , 我們可以看到一些粒子似乎缺少的空隙 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的原理 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家將已有的結構作為子集 , 尋找較大、較對稱的形狀 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	較大的圖形便能讓我們預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 這應該和弱力很相像 , 只是比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這個載荷集 , 並考慮到關於物質粒子的奇怪現象:在六度載荷空間中 , 物質的第二代和第三代相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子不是由其六個載荷所辨識出來的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間上 , 它們會彼此疊加 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能對每個粒子分配出獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後在八度空間中旋轉看看整個模式是什麼樣子
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代 , 是由一個叫做 「 三重性 」 的對稱產生 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外說謊團體e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	李群是光滑曲線形的248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案的每一點都能對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀就能描述宇宙如何在最小的尺度下運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種圖形在八度載荷空間中是非常精緻的美麗 , 它可以總結成千上萬的這些基本粒子間的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的平面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到這個包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們可以在八度空間沿一個對稱軸 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 就像任何統一一樣 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 那裡的新粒子是這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	有20個空白點應該有新粒子 , 其中兩個已經填滿了帕翠西亞姆粒子 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	根據它們圖案的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是比如希格斯粒子 , 但它們有顏色載荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新粒子中填滿了這個圖案 , 讓我們得到完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學裡最美的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美麗物體的理論有一個奇妙的前景可以從最小的尺度描述粒子互動的真相
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個被數學描述的概念並不是新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫道: 「 大自然的偉大一本書 , 一直敞開我們的凝視 , 都是用數學的語言寫出來的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何形體 , 沒有它在人體上是不可能理解它的任何一個字的 ; 沒有這些字 , 會在黑暗的迷宮中盤旋 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著用伽利略的指引來描述粒子物理的數學用的只有三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但確保數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學一起 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個不斷成長的e8珊瑚 , 每個可能的地點都相互作用著 , 根據一個美麗的圖案來描述 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	使用大型強子對撞機之類的新機器 , 我們或許能看到大自然是否使用這種e8圖案或不一樣的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現符合e8圖案的粒子那就太酷了
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新粒子 , 但不符合這個圖案 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對e8理論不利 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是很危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論及其它類似的理論都是很長的點擊 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個做了很多辛苦的工作 , 知道大部分這些想法可能最後都不是真的 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很多的無知 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司一樣
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就像任何大型投資一樣 , 在失敗的情況下 , 心理上很難拋棄這條研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果沒有用 , 就得要丟掉它 , 嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	要維持理智並在不確定中獲得快樂 , 唯一的方法就是在生命中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能去過一個平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛、衝浪中找到平衡 , 用我三個載荷的方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	如此一來 , 即使我研究的物理沒有任何成就 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年 , 我住在毛伊島 , 一個很美的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是我父母最大的謎題之一 , 我如何能隨時活下來 , 卻不願投入任何相似的全職工作 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的照片 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景色都很相似 , 但有些地方卻不太一樣 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	因為這曾是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種很不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心房租 , 讓我把時間花在做我喜歡做的事情上 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 過著游牧的生活很艱苦 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 讓我在生活中保持平衡 , 我一直很高興 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的陪伴 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以 , 我很高興被邀請到ted來 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能明白其中的2% , 但我還是很喜歡它 。 所以我會發出愚蠢的聲音 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論:我習慣了珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 至少有少數人感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它能把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以你是不是說我們應該把宇宙的核心看成是最小的事物有可能就是e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 有沒有一個尺碼在最小的尺度上 , 或者是......
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	gl:我剛剛給你們看的圖形與我們所知的基本粒子物理學已經相對應了一種非常美麗的圖形 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那個就是我說我們很肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀與e8圖案有很明顯的相似之處 , 可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點圖案實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性這些圖案會在我們經歷的時空中扭曲、移動、舞蹈
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了所有這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但是弦理論家 , 如我所理解的 , 用較小的弦波振動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在其中振動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何想像在e8之間的電子呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不對稱是e8型態的一種對稱
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當形狀在時空中移動的時候 , 它在扭轉 。 當它移動的軌跡是粒子 。 所以它的大小是e8 , 那跟電子的大小又有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要那張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它會更大嗎 ? 它會更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格:據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以會縮減到最小的尺寸 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有的可能性都在同時展開和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是為什麼我用珊瑚的比喻來類比 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的進入方式是 , 它就像每個時空點的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀在經過曲線的表面時會扭曲的方向 , 形狀會扭曲 , 基本粒子就是它們自己 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	通過量子場理論 , 他們把自己當作點點 , 然後以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能把這張照片做得更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:沒關係 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它激起了我們的興趣 , 我當然希望更了解這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	非常謝謝你來到這裡 。 這真是太吸引人了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	很傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍•古德爾談到tacare以及她的其他社區專案 , 這專案能協助非洲各地的居民和受到威脅的動物一起生活 。
