jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 諸如此類
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以這樣說 , 晚安 , 晚安 , 晚安但我們也可以--噢 , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , oooh , oooh , oooh
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所接到的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到的是從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一群 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今晚我想從昨天哲學家離開的地方開始挑選這場演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇的三歲靈長類小孩selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也曾聽過透過基因圖譜 , 人類人類的歷史、家族樹的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	已故的古生物學家路易斯.李奇 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	這在當時是相當了不起的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在已經有點普遍了 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	從化石 , 從肌肉依附的形狀 , 你可以大量的判斷出那些肌肉的外觀 , 這些肌肉外觀是什麼樣子的 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 他就是想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張--這是個很普遍的理論如果我們在現存的近親中找到相似的行為模式或相同的行為模式 , 如今人類 , 也許這些行為是在七百萬年前左右出現的 , 人類和人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特質從古老、古老的過去帶給我們 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	假如你看了今日談及人類進化的教科書你會經常看到人們對於早期人類行為的推測根據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類行為
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們跟我們很相似比其他生物在這場ted大會上我們都聽過
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以對我來說 , 評論黑猩猩和我們有何相似之處 , 在牠們行為的某些方面 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他或她的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給他們取名字 。 他們可以活到60歲以上 , 雖然我們認為大部分的孩子在野外不會活到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	莫瑞爾先生 。 母鳥十一或十二歲時 , 會生下第一胎 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	每五六年 , 她就生了一個小孩 , 很長一段時間的孩童依賴期 , 那時是養育嬰兒 , 晚上和母親一起睡 , 背靠背 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的童年對黑猩猩是很重要的 , 就跟我們人類一樣 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同動物的演化過程中不斷變得更複雜 , 因此我們發現 , 學習在個體的生命歷史中扮演著越來越重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 不同的使用工具的行為 , 已經在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中研究過這些行為 , 從一個世代傳下來 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 來描述這些使用工具的行為 , 作為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩們沒有口說的語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有很豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多和我們相似 , 甚至與我們相同 , 在相同的情境下形成的 。 與擁抱的對比 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、拍彼此 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	它們會大吃一驚 , 會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會 , 我們發現很多很多例子都是同情 , 例如愛情和真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 就像我們人類一樣 , 牠們也有天生的黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們能夠極度殘暴 , 甚至有點原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些極具攻擊性的行為 , 大部分都是針對社區團體的對象 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們非常激進 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經讓我們明白 , 人類和動物王國之間並沒有一條明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條線非常的模糊 , 隨著我們進行更多的觀察 , 它變得更加的模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外的複雜社會生活的黑猩猩 , 幫助我們發現 , 人類是其中的一員 , 卻沒有分離 , 和我們共享這個星球的驚人動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以發現黑猩猩 , 和世界上其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 照片上頭是哥倫比森林的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時我飛越整個地區 , 大約16年前 , 那時我了解到 , 在這個公園之外 , 在1960年 , 幾乎完全沒有被破壞的森林沿著坦尼加的東岸 , 那是一個小小的 , 30平方公園的國家公園 , 我突然想到一個問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 那時 , 住在國家公園附近的人正掙扎著要生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	那裡住的人比土地還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	由於土地和剛果湖的難民數量不斷增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	窮人買不起他們買的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了我們的計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	改善公園附近村莊的人們的生活方式非常整合 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從十二個村莊開始 , 現在是二十四個村莊 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討 , 包括樹木的護士、農耕的方式 , 如今最適合這片荒蕪、幾乎像沙漠一樣的山上土地 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制與預防土壤流失的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地 , 這樣在兩年內 , 他們就能再有生產力了 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	協助村民從井裡取得乾淨的水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信和一些婦女們合作 , 提供她們提供微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地 , 我們有大約95%的貸款回來 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	授權給女性 , 與教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 這樣她們才能完成中學 , 讓我明白 , 在全世界各地明白 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 保育會發生什麼事 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	農夫們住在這24個村落裡 , 而不是以一群白種人的身分來研究一群猴子順便一提 , 現在坦桑尼亞的工作人員很多是坦尚尼亞人但當我們開始坦尚尼亞造林計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞的團隊就進入了村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一支坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民對話 , 詢問他們感興趣的 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白山坡的上層次是樹木 , 所以土壤流失和土石流 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這塊區域遠在國家公園之外 , 向外延伸 , 進入所有這些被摧毀的土地 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村落有更好的生活標準他們真的同意將百分之十到二十的高地邊緣的土地放一邊如此一來 , 當樹木長回來的時候黑猩猩們就有了自己的葉門走廊他們可以通過這些地方與國家公園外的其他殘存族群互動
so tacare is a success .	所以坦尚尼亞造林計劃是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其它地區複製 , 其它野外地區的面臨極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲的問題 , 正如我們在ted的前幾天所討論的 , 都是大問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮的問題非常嚴重 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量人住在不太肥沃的土地上 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 留下土壤 , 成為侵蝕的風 , 因為絕望的人口減少了越來越多的樹木 , 讓他們自己和家人種植食物 , 會發生什麼事 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	還有另一個問題 , 不只在非洲 , 還在發展中國家 , 到處都是 , 我們對地球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華.威爾森曾說過 , 如果在這個星球上每個人的生活標準只有歐洲或美國人的平均生活水準 , 我們需要三顆新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們有四個說法 , 但我們沒有 , 我們只有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	那會發生什麼事呢 ? 我的意思是 , 這個問題在這兒 , 我們可說是最聰明的生物 , 即便是走在地球上 , 還是擁有超凡的大腦 , 這些科技都已經被這些ted研討會給闡釋了 , 而我們卻在毀滅我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	全世界的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 通常會坐下來問自己: 「 這樣的決定對我們的七代子孫有什麼影響 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 重大的決定 , 我在這裡談的 , 並不是非洲 , 但 , 已開發國家的重大決定通常涉及數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是基於 「 這會如何影響下一次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各處旅行 , 談到黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 談到牠們消失的森林 , 我發現越來越多非洲的問題可能會出現在先前殖民的剝削上 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲談話 , 在美國談話 , 到亞洲去 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我說的那種 , 我指的是污染
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們所呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害著我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水可能是本世紀面臨的最關鍵的議題之一 , 世界各地的水正在被污染 , 被農業、工業和家庭用化學物污染 , 這些化學物仍然在世界各地被噴灑著 , 似乎沒有經驗來獲取過去的利益 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯的效應會更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤流失 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有不斷燃燒的石化燃料 , 還有其他溫室氣體 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 人們開始認為我們的氣候出了問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混在一起了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	受影響較嚴重的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱變得更糟了 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	而當雨來的時候 , 常會導致洪水、增加災難 , 以及貧窮、飢餓 , 和疾病的惡性循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在土地無法支援的地區的人數太貧窮無法購買食物因為土地都被降解了
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以當最後一棵樹被砍掉時 , 你會看到沙漠化的現象 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種事情不只在非洲 , 全世界都是如此
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們好像失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	好吧 , 你認為在這聰明的大腦之間 , 可能有某種隔閡嗎 ? ted科技的例證和人類的心靈 ? 從科學的角度來說 , 愛和同情的角度來說 , 有某種隔閡嗎 ? 是否存在某種斷層 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們不是很沮喪、很冷漠、很痛苦 , 或很憤怒 。 他們說的或多或少是一樣的: 「 我們會這樣想 , 因為我們覺得你們已經妥協了未來 , 而我們卻無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每一次我看著他們 , 就會想到從我還是個年紀開始 , 我們已經傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我就感到絕望了 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這也導致了我們稱為根與芽的計畫 , 起始於坦尚尼亞 , 目前已經擴散到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它有象徵性的意義 。 根有堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看似微小 ; 要抵達太陽 , 它們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所有的問題 , 像是環境和社會問題 。 它是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人能夠突破現狀 , 讓所有生物都變得更好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的信息是:我們每一個人每天都會做出改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在這房間裡的每一個人 , 我們都有一個選擇 , 來決定要做什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	那些非常貧窮的人沒有選擇 。 這取決於我們要改變現狀 , 使窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體會選出三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論是在城市或鄉村 , 哪種計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	基本上 , 我們有從幼稚園到大學的專案計畫 , 有越來越多的成年人開始著屬於自己的根與芽的群組 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體在他們之間選擇 , 三個不同的專案 , 讓這個更美好的世界 , 承認這些不同的問題彼此連結 , 並互相衝突 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的其中一項計畫 , 就是協助他們自己的社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能做到 , 他們就能籌集資金來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的專案之一 , 是幫助動物們 , 不僅是野生動物、家養動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個計畫是幫助這個我們共有的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	這一切都是在學習和平共存的訊息 , 學習在我們自己、在我們的家庭、社區、國家、文化之間、文化之間、文化之間、在我們與自然世界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能繼續破壞它的速度 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這一個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	僅僅挑選其中一兩個在非洲的計畫根與芽的團體正在進行一項或兩個計畫在坦尚尼亞 , 烏干達 , 肯亞 , 南非 , 剛果 , 獅子山共和國 , 喀麥隆和其它的團體 。 如我說的 , 目前有97個國家在做這件事 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 他們種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 有雞賣的雞蛋 , 只為了一點點的錢 , 或用這些蛋來餵飽他們的家人 , 讓他們感到自豪和自主 , 因為他們不再無助 , 不再依靠他人的蔬菜和雞隻 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些早期士兵的心理幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這類的專案 , 是讓他們自己脫離困境 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次地 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在根本就沒有更多根與芽了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要要素 , 讓年長的孩子和年紀較小的孩子溝通 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	還有未受懷孕之類的事物 , 讓年輕人更能傾聽其他青年 , 而非成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 我在世界各地都會被問到這個問題: 「 珍 , 你見過很多很糟糕的事情 , 你見過你的黑猩猩數量減少了一百萬隻 , 在本世紀初 , 到現在不超過十五萬隻 , 許多其他動物也一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林不斷消失 , 曾經有森林的地方也消失 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣子的研討會 , 並且沒有希望 , 對吧 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中之一是人類的大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我最後非常興奮 , 能來談談堆肥式的公廁 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我其中一個嗜好 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把所有的水往馬桶裡沖 , 都很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到能再生能源非常重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩、孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們身為世界上的精英 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以選擇如何過日子 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用這個問題來做這些選擇 , 它會如何影響我周圍的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我的孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 等等
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	人類的大腦 , 再搭配上人類的心臟 , 我們和世界各地的聯手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted協助我們更好的原因 , google也協助我們 , esri也幫我們繪製了gombe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們來把它們連結起來 , 它也開始發生了 , 對吧 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你已經聽說了 , 它已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這樣的改變 , 這樣的轉變 。 如果我們關心未來 , 就要看到我們必須看到的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個原因是希望大自然有驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以讓一塊完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要有時間 , 或許還能讓它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而坦尚尼亞造林計劃就是其中一個例子
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你 , 哪裡有一隻看似死去的樹木如果你停止砍伐它們而你就不需要因為你有很多木屑而在五年之內你就有了一棵三十呎長的樹
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎都滅絕的邊緣可以再有第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這很有啟發性 。 這也帶到了我最後一類希望的領域 , 在過去兩天中我們聽到了很多這樣的事:不屈不撓的人類精神 。 人類堅毅的決心 , 人類堅毅的韌性 , 所以那些你認為被貧窮、疾病所擊垮的人 , 可以自己脫身 , 有時可以幫助他們在社會上的一部分 , 讓他們成為改變世界的人 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	試想一下 , 來自非洲的一兩個人很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但很顯然的 , 納爾遜•曼德拉出現於17年的實體勞工身上 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著這不可思議的寬恕去原諒 , 讓他帶領他的國家擺脫了種族隔離 , 沒有血戰 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的薩維瓦對巨型石油公司雖然全世界的人竭盡所能 , 卻被處死了
people like this are so inspirational .	像這類的人都很鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是年輕非洲人需要的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境角色模型 , 我今天也聽到了一些模型 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感謝這個機會再次分享這個訊息 , 給ted的每個人 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們中的一些人可以聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後我要說的是那位經營這整個會議的年輕女子 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她拿著她的證書變得很興奮 。 她是根與芽的產物 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 它協助她做她在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	這對我來說非常興奮 , 能見到她 , 並看到一個例子 , 當年輕人被賦權時 , 能採取行動的機會 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 真正成為明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩有一些關於海洋和生活中的塑膠污染的艱苦真相 , 和一些如何從塑膠漩渦中解放自己的想法 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球性議題、綠色、藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜.柯恩:關於塑膠污染的棘手真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在跟塑膠袋合作 , 我把塑膠袋剪下來 , 再縫合成我作品作品的主要材料 , 過去二十年來 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我將它們轉變為二、三維的部分、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	大約八年後 , 我和塑膠合作 , 我有些工作開始發財 , 分解成更小的塑膠塊 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣 , 是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	一旦我對塑膠有更多的知識我就明白這是一件壞事
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠分解成小塊是壞事 , 因為它永遠是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	而我們發現的是 , 很多的塑膠都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾桶和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是很多人的第一個反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去把這玩意清乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我提出了一個計劃 , 和一艘貨櫃船以及兩艘退休的捕魚船船 , 一輛起重機 , 一台起重機 , 和一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我打算要去垃圾漩渦 , 提高大家對這個議題的認知 , 然後開始把塑膠拿出來做成碎片 , 把它冷藏起來 , 把它們當作開發中的材料來當建材 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過垃圾漩渦垃圾環流的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 在做這件事時 , 我發現 , 要清理塑膠 , 和全世界每天產生的量是非常小的比例 , 且我得要回去看整體狀況 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更重要的是:我們需要找到一種方式來關掉表面 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要削減使用一次就丟棄的塑膠 , 每天進入海洋環境 , 以全球的規模 , 來減少使用一次性的使用 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	看到這一點 , 我也意識到我很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只在乎塑膠你也在試著想像在太平洋中間的那些我現在知道有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦遍及世界上5個主要海洋
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我關心的不只是這些塑膠垃圾的漩渦還有這些超市的塑膠漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會到超級市場去買 , 我所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都被塑膠包裝在塑膠裡 , 甚至在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠還有從塑膠中滲出的毒素到我們的身體裡
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他人一起研究這個問題 , 我們建立了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫正在進行 , 但有些計畫很基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的 , 80%到90%的海洋殘骸是塑膠 , 那我們何不稱它為塑膠 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	資源回收--每個人的書都結束了 , 說到永續經營和綠色回收的理念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你只要在垃圾桶裡放些東西 , 你就不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	這件事的現實是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	特別是當談到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只能降級回收或燒掉 , 或運到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它是一回事 , 然後變成更便宜的東西 , 而玻璃瓶又是一層玻璃瓶又或是能再次被使用 , 塑膠瓶永遠不會再是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是一個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們在看並要求人們思考的事是我們在 「 減量、再利用、回收三 」 前面加上第四個r , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	總之 , 盡量拒絕用過即丟的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案有 ; 有些是非常老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在在收集這些很酷的pyrexcon容器 , 不用那些容器和保鮮盒 , 可以儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我正在為自己和我的家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要找到一個不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 如果你要去旅行 , 而你忘了帶個不銹鋼瓶裝水 , 而不是收購塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想對在座的各位說 , 我知道你們對這個問題了解很多──這對海洋是很大的問題 , 但這是身為消費者所造成的問題 , 我們可以解決的 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	藉由提高對這個問題的認知和教導人們選擇其他替代選項來解決這個問題 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 盡可能地選擇用過的塑膠替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些幹道切成海洋 , 如此一來 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這張圖是來自麻省理工學院的pattiemaes的實驗室 , 由pranvmetry帶領的 , 是ted的buzz 。 它是一個可以穿戴的裝置 , 上面有深度的互動空間 。 想像一下 , 「 關鍵報告 」 和一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技、科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和帕納•米特利展示展示第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直很感興趣的問題是 , 我們能否演化或發展出第六感 , 一種能夠讓我們無縫接觸、容易取得代謝 , 或可能存在的資訊 , 能夠協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們遇到了什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們有些人可能認為現今的手機不就已經有這個功能了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會拒絕 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted與某人見面時--當然 , 這是今年最佳的社交場所--你不會和某人握手然後說: 「 你能等一下嗎 ? 我拿出我的手機和google嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者當你到超級市場站在那個巨大的不同類型的衛生紙上時 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 上網去瀏覽器 , 來決定這些不同的衛生紙是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組一直在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能用一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 卻不會要求用戶改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新努力 , 最成功的努力 , 到目前為止 , 這工作仍然是個過程 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我手上有裝置 , 我們已經把它和架上下的零件拼湊起來 , 順便一提 , 目前這個時候的成本是三百五十美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我帶著一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 攜帶式的電池動力投影系統 , 還有鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些裝置在口袋裡跟我的手機溝通 , 扮演著溝通和計算的裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片裡 , 我們看到我的學生 , 帕納•密斯 , 他真的是實施這個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何平面上 , 開始用他的手和投影在他面前的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤這四隻手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 你可能認得到 , 他戴著簡單的標記帽 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且辨識出他的任何手勢舉例來說 , 他能直接飛到一個長灘的地圖 , 放大和縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統還能辨識出具象徵性的姿勢 , 比如 「 拍一張照片 」 的姿勢 , 然後拍一張你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆上投影他所拍攝的所有照片 , 一邊整理這些照片 , 然後將它們放大 , 一邊使用自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	你們中一些人在兩年前就在這裡 , 看到了傑夫•漢所做的示範 , 你們可能在想: 「 這不是很像微軟的平面電腦嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢來互動 , 包括雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	這裡的差別在於你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面前 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他表面可以用 , 和這個投影出來的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置完全可攜帶 , 也可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個不同點是它是完全流動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同點在於 , 大眾生產中 , 明天要比現今的手機要貴 , 且設計的包裝並不會更大 , 看起來會比我脖子上掛的版本更時髦 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除此之外 , 讓你們其中一些人活在 「 關鍵報告 」 裡 , 看起來還很酷的 「 tomcruise 」 裡 , 我們對這個裝置感到很興奮的原因是 , 它真的可以成為第六感裝置的其中一個裝置 , 讓你知道你面前的任何資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕納進入超市他要買一些紙巾
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品 , 這個系統可以辨識出他撿到的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他能詢問額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	在他的個人標準來看 , 這裡的選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想買加入最多漂白劑的衛生紙而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就能得到亞馬遜書局的評分 。 它會直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是juan的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順便說一下 , 在亞馬遜 , 評分很棒 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻了這本書的網頁 , 看得到更多關於這本書的資訊 , 像是讀者評論的資訊 , 像是他最愛的評論家的評論 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到特定的一頁 , 他能找到我們的朋友所寫的註解 , 讓他能得到更多關於那一頁內容的資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙時 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以用影片來表示事件發生的狀況 , 你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這個比較有爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted和某人互動時 , 也許你可以看見標籤的字雲 , 和那人相關的字眼在他們的部落格和個人網頁上 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣 ,
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的航班延遲了 , 登機門也改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道現在的時間 , 這就跟在手臂上畫一個手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前開發出第六感能夠讓我們無縫地取得關於我們可能遇到的事物的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 就像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很多掌聲 , 因為我認為他在過去三個月來其實沒睡多少 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也對他不太滿意 。

and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 , 也許十年後我們會帶著植入腦的終極第六感來到這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyisrodriguez和aichaelwafi有一個強大的友誼誕生於2001年9月11日世貿中心在世貿中心攻擊事件中被殺害 ; elwafi的兒子z-zussaoui被定罪於攻擊中 , 並為期的一句話服務 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911修復法:找到寬恕 , 友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大家認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現在卻覺得很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現我的兒子是在世界貿易中心 , 那是在2001年9月11日的早晨 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否曾過世 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們國家將會做的事 , 以我們兒子的名義──我的丈夫、奧蘭多 , 以及我和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到-雖然 , 很震驚 , 很可怕的震驚 , 我們生活中的可怕的爆炸 , 真的沒被報復 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖主義的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判處死刑如果罪名成立 , 我和我的丈夫公開反對他說的話 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些以及透過人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者家屬團結在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控的時候 , 走過來 , 我心想: 「 一個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	總有一天 , 當我更強壯時 , 我想和那女人見面 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲慟中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或說我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我馬上就得到了同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子所被指控的事 , 她沒有得到那種同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦和我的相同 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月相遇 , 現在aicha會告訴你這一切是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichael-wafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui之母
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我去接觸受害人的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭認識 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這群人中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我從她眼中看到她是母親 , 跟我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我常受苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結了婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲時失去了第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	zacarias的故事實在是太過分了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然苦難 , 因為我兒子好像他活著 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否受酷刑 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以這就是我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的苦難對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須要親手操作 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性 , 而是為了我們 , 為我們女人 , 為了我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年輕的穆斯林女孩談 , 這樣他們才不會接受和自己意願結婚的女生 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 盡我所能讓他們結婚、受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我站在各位面前的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha身上學到很多東西 , 從那天起 , 我們第一次見到其他家庭成員--那是安全的私人會面 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 而老實說 , 我們害怕當時國家裡的超級愛國主義--我們這些成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	接著 , 她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們想和她見面 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們希望對方得到什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字之前 , 我們已經擁抱和哭泣 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們就圍成一圈 , 提供協助 , 讓人們感受到這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha從頭開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我兒子是有罪還是無辜的 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我對你們家人的遭遇有多麼不好意思 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 且我覺得只要有犯罪 , 就應該要被公平對待、被懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以這種方式向我們伸出援手我想說這是一個破冰的過程
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 都和人類連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午完結時 , 大概是午餐後的三小時 , 我們覺得好像彼此認識了很久 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不單止是她可以如此的寬容即使在當時的處境和當時的處境下 , 和在她兒子身上所發生的 , 還有她所經歷的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有見過一個人 , 心中有著如此艱苦的人生 , 來自我自己那完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我很珍惜它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是關於害怕他人 , 但踏出這一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這並不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	還能跟誰見面呢 ? 我不知道 , 還是跟我很不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以得出結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	安德森:我想說我們得要試著認識其他人 , 其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 , 你的心念也要寬容 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定是包容的 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天 , 我們都能以和平的態度生活在一起 , 互相尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這就是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多地方無法取得乾淨的飲用水了 。 michaelprichard對它做了點什麼 , 發明可攜帶的生命安全過濾器 , 在幾秒鐘之內 , 就能讓最令人振奮的水源喝水 。 2009年的tedlobal做了一個很棒的演示 。

michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	麥可•普立德的水過濾器變得很骯髒 , 可飲用 。

the first thing is water .	第一是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都享受著在研討會裡提供的水 , 在過去幾天 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得它的來源是安全的 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果沒有呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	然後統計學家會說你們之中有一半的人現在有腹瀉的病痛 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談過很多關於統計和提供所有人安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎還沒撐過去 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用當前的想法 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法想像要解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以 , 我們、政府 , 和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想和各位分享 , 透過不同的思考方式 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 世界上的一萬三千人正受著腹瀉的折磨 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛剛死去 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我很憤怒 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們多數人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節過後的隔天 , 我看著海嘯摧殘的新聞 , 在電視上不斷播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝被污染的水 , 或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這一直困擾著我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風往美國衝撞了一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做些什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要五天才能把水送到超級大的地方嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相開槍 , 搶著電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時 , 我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	我在我的車庫裡待了很多時間 , 接下來幾個禮拜、幾個月 , 我在廚房裡也花了很多時間 , 對我妻子感到很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過一些失敗的原型之後 , 我終於做出了這個 , 生命安全瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談談科學方面 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水機之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這絕對會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生命薩佛的孔洞是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西走完了 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我來示範一下給你們看 。
would you like to see that ?	你們想看到嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我把所有時間都準備好了 , 所以我猜我應該要這麼做 。

so someone's done that up .	所以有人就這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	美好的牛津城市 , 我已經從河裡取了一些水 , 溪流這裡流過來 , 就是這些水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我覺得 , 你知道嗎 , 如果我們身在孟加拉一帶洪水區的中間 , 水就不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以我拿了一些東西來加進去 。
and this is from my pond .	這是從我家裡池塘出來的 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞到那個 , 攝影師的氣味 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們要把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	麥可.普立查:好 , 我們還有一些從污水處理場流出的 。

put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 。 就是這樣 。

so we're just going to put that in there as well .	所以我們也把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶的成效非常簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水往上爬 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個水壺來展示給大家看 。 讓我們來一點點大便 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這樣還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 那我要把這些非常骯髒的水放進這裏 。 你還想喝個東西嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 來吧 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	稍微抽幾次 , 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	那就是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶拉出來 , 無菌的飲用水就會跑出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	就像這樣 。 注意到電力 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那很安全、無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	來吧克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	味道是什麼 ?

okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	世界各地有幾千人使用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它可用六千公升的水 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	如果過期了 , 使用故障安全技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	將內裝拿出來 , 換一個新的進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	再6 , 000公升對6 , 000公升就好 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看這些應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	幾個禮拜過後 , 我們建立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到營地取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	要是兩萬人聚集在營地會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病傳播 , 需要更多的資源
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	這個問題會自我複製 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考模式 , 運送這些資訊 , 人們可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要天然災害才可行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工程 , 實在太昂貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你計算機運算時 , 你的運算能力不夠 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡是 「 用不同想法 」 的一部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程來運送 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費除鹽 , 運送到那裡 , 並傾倒在山上、河川 , 和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 鄰近水源的地方 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它消毒 。 我們要怎麼做呢 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者我們也可以用這一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 裝在五加侖罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	處理二萬五千公升的水 , 足夠給一個四人的家庭使用三年 。
and how much does it cost ?	這要多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約要半分錢去跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 換種思考方式 , 在用途中處理水 , 母親和孩子們不再需要每天走四小時來取得水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的資源取得它 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只要花八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目的 , 讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	要把這個概念納入考量 , 英國政府每年花大約120億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼會停在這裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	結果是每年因此受苦的三十五億人 , 每年死亡的兩百萬孩童會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashdown聲稱我們現在生活在歷史上的一個時刻 , 權力正在以前所未有的方式改變 。 在一場tedxbrusels的精彩演講中他排除了他所看到的三大全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化 ,
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是出名的英國詩人在十九世紀末所寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	它在1930年代被告知要在邱吉爾的大腦中迴盪 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這麼寫的: 「 夏天的山丘上 , 躺在那堆溪流裡 , 我聽到遙遠的鼓聲 , 我聽見遙遠的鼓聲就像在夢中聽見的一樣 , 遠近 , 接近地 , 越來越低的聲響在路上 , 親愛的 , 親愛的 , 親愛的食物 , 走向粉末 , 很快就要死掉了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	想寫詩的人 , 這首詩的題目是 " 購物館小姐 " , 由一名寄主所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但是 , 豪斯曼所領悟到的 , 你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽過 , 那是十九世紀長久、炎熱、無天的夏天 , 近在一個世紀 , 我們即將進入史上最可怕的時期之一 , 那時 , 權力可以改變 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士這些日子總是伴隨著騷動偶爾也會有血
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責 , 如果你喜歡 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當那些已建立的秩序權力開始改變的時刻 , 以及這個世界的新樣貌 , 那些存在於世界上的新權力正在開始成形 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些也是我們現在明顯看到的 , 幾乎都是非常混亂的時代 , 極度艱難的時代 , 很多時候都是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 這在本世紀發生過一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你們可能會說 , 上一次發生的狀況 , 和霍斯曼後來的感受 , 和邱吉爾的感受 , 是因為權力從舊國 , 歐洲的舊勢力跨越大西洋到美國的新興勢力──美國本世紀初的開始 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那個時候歐洲人過時的權力被人用來操控兩場血腥的災難的事件在上個世紀第一部份就是兩次世界大戰
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經說過他們是歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更精確的描述他們的方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活的次數之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個層面是我想談的一些新的層面從來沒有像現在這樣發生過
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談世界上發生的權力移轉 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	現今正在發生的是 , 在某種意義上 , 可怕 , 因為從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們見過橫向的權力移轉希臘轉到羅馬還有發生在歐洲文明的權力移轉但我們卻看到了一些不一樣的東西
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只是從國家轉向國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也是直向運動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今所發生的是 , 被推廣的權力 , 被關在法律的制度裡 , 在國家的制度下 , 已經被大量的運算在全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力我們談的是全球化市場 , 但實際上是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級 , 權力受到責任 , 受到法律的牽制 , 卻沒有在國際舞台上 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台 , 現在的電力掌握:網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢改變的力量 , 大筆流通的金錢 , 現在已經是交易所需的三十二倍 , 如果你願意 , 金融的推動者 , 近期間 , 已經把我們的膝蓋送到大型企業的電力發電廠 , 比以前更大的預算還要多了 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些人住在一個全球化的空間 , 很大程度上是沒有規範的 , 沒有法律規範的 , 人們可以自由地行動 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	這些都是強大而有力的時刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些最有權力的人在沒有限制的情況下運作 , 但在歷史上 , 所學到的教訓 , 就是 , 遲早 , 沒有受到法律規範的空間 , 不僅是你想要的國際貿易、網路等等 。 還包括你不希望國際犯罪、跨國恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11的揭露是:即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 你的太空人可以在一個九月的早晨攻擊你甚至是城市中最具代表性的象徵 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	有人說四百萬美金中大約有百分之六十被用來資助911恐怖攻擊的錢是通過雙子星大樓的機構讓911摧毀
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這樣的空間大眾旅遊、網路、衛星廣播設施來避開毒物這就是摧毀我們的系統和路線
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早晚晚晚晚晚晚晚晚晚晚晚晚晚晚 , 歷史的規則是權力到哪裡去統治 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	所以如果這是我相信的 , 我們時代的一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代所面臨的挑戰就是把統治者帶上國際舞台 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信我們眼前的幾十年 , 將會是更大或更小的亂流 , 我們有能力實現目標:把統治者帶到全球空間中 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在談政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便說一句 , 我自己的觀點是 , 各位先生女士 , 這種觀點不太可能引發更多聯合國機構 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就必須把它發明出來 。
the world needs an international forum .	這個世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	國際行動需要一個合法的手段 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當涉及到國際舞台的管理我認為這不會發生在建立更多的聯合國機構
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	會因為強大的力量聚集在一起 , 做出以治療為基礎的系統 , 以條約為基礎的協定 , 來統治這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你仔細觀察 , 就會發現這些事正在發生 , 已經開始出現 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約為底的組織 , 完全以合約為基礎的組織 , 卻強大到能夠持有最強大的力量 , 即便是美國 , 仍有必要的條約 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:掙扎著要創造一個合約為底的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在我們知道 , 我們必須組建一個能夠把統治權帶到金融空間的機構 , 給金融市場 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而這就是二十國集團因而建立的 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等下會再回到這個問題 , 那就是當你把最有權力的人集合在一起 , 在以條約為基礎的制度上做規則 , 來填補政府的空間 , 那弱者會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 待會兒我們會回到這問題上
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一條訊息是 , 如果你多次通過這些亂流 , 或多或少造成動盪 , 那麼 , 我們的成功將會大量依賴我們的能力 , 把合理的管理帶到全球空間 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看看這個現象開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 還橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你或許會說 , 文明的歷史就是人類的文明集聚在海邊 , 最先到達地中海的物種 , 近期西方後大西洋的興起時期就有越多的物種 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是更根本的權力移轉 , 廣義的說法 , 遠離大西洋岸周圍的國家 , 和太平洋岸的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這要從經濟實力開始 , 但一直是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他正在成長的政策中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為 , 這其實不算是從西方移向東邊 , 有什麼不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我想 , 根據它的價值 , 美國會保持地球上最強的國家未來十年、十五年 , 但她掌握她的權力的環境已經徹底改變 , 已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正走出過去的50年 , 最不尋常的這段時間 , 在這個世界上 , 我們有一個完全獨立的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每個指南針都要仰賴它的位置 , 來華盛頓這個世界 , 由一個巨大霸主來決定 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上卻不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在所發生的事 , 是歷史上更正常的情況 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你將會看到一個多極化的世界出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國一直是我們世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家 , 但他們會是這個日益擴大的多極世界中最有權力的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你就會開始看到在中國建立權力的替代中心 , 當然 , 我自己的猜想是中國要追求偉大 , 並不容易 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	這很慘烈 , 因為中國在自由經濟之後將她的社會民主化了 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個議題的主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到的是印度 , 巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	對於我們歐洲人來說 , 世界越來越像是19世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀:一個英國的外交大臣坎寧 , 曾形容它是 「 歐洲人的權力協調 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一種平衡 , 一種五面向的平衡
britain always played to the balance .	英國人總是處於平衡之中 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國就和維也納及羅馬合作 , 來維也納和它取得平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在這個由獨立世界主宰的時期 , 你有固定的聯盟 , 北約組織 , 華沙聯盟 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的兩極性就意味著結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力多極的兩極性就意味著改變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們即將進入的世界 , 我們將看到越來越多的同盟國沒有被修復 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交大臣坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有一個共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	即便在西方國家 , 我們仍會逐漸看到 , 我們仍必須向外伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 和他人結盟 , 只要我們想要把事情做對 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞 , 西方無法獨自完成這件事 , 我們必須加入其他人 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須引進阿拉伯聯盟
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方國家嘗試自己做事的最後一次而我們並沒有成功
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我想我們已經達到400年以上的開端了我說四百年來因為這是西方國家力量、西方國家體系和西方價值的終結
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能整合起來 , 它能在世界的每個角落提出並丟棄 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以上次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家組織了布雷頓森林機構世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金問題解決了
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須接到別人的電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須建立一個g20集團
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我來做個預測 , 這可能會更嚇人 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經到了西方國家400年的終結 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國絕對不會參與什麼在世界上建立和平的活動 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	哦 , 對嗎 ? 那為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷區之下服務 , 在世界上的藍色旗幟之下 , 服務於聯合國的指令 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	到底什麼是能解決索馬利亞海盜最大的海軍陸戰 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍憲法
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是重商的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要保持航道的開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	我們會越來越常和我們不共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但當下 , 我們會共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是個全新的角度來看這個正在浮現的世界
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	這裡是第三個因素 , 它完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們的現代世界 , 由於網際網路 , 因為人們在此談論的人們 , 每件事都有關聯 。
we are now interdependent .	我們是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是以國家作為單獨的個體 , 在以前從未如此過 , 從未如此過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關係 , 一直都存在著 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被親密地結合在一起了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 24小時後 , 法國戴高樂機場就會出問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉很多次崩潰
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原發生火災非洲的食物暴動
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們彼此間都有深深的連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	也就是說 , 一個國家單獨行動 , 而不是與其他人聯繫 , 不再與其他人合作 , 不再是一個可行的論點 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動並不侷限於自己 , 也不足以讓國家去掌控它自己的領土 , 因為超越國家的影響已經開始影響著他們內在的一切 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我當時還是個年輕的軍人在英國最後一次的小型帝國大戰 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	在那時 , 我的國家的防禦是一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	敵人就在城牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人就在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在我想談談我國家的國防 , 我必須和衛生署談談 , 因為傳染疾病對我的安全是威脅 , 我必須和農業部談談 , 因為糧食安全對我的國家是威脅 , 我必須和工業部談 , 因為高科技的基礎設施很脆弱 , 現在對我們的敵人進行攻擊 , 如同網路戰爭對我們的敵人一樣 , 我必須和那些在我們國家對我們的家來說 , 那些在我們國家 , 已經進入我們國家的房子的人 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	國家的安全不再只和軍人和國防有關
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力是把自制力固定在一起的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
