it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴我們 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直架構 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 縱向層級制度 , 專門分配任務 , 指揮結構 , 完全就是錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在座的各位 , 各位先生女士 , 在座的各位 , 企業知道我們時代的典範結構是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	這是你對於網路的能力 , 很重要 , 無論是在你的政府還是外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	對了 , 別問我第一條法則和第二條法則是什麼因為我還沒發明出來 ; 第三條法則總是比較好聽 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	shown的第三法則是 , 在現代 , 每件事都有關連最重要的是 , 你能和別人做什麼 , 最重要的是你能做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	無論你是政府 , 還是軍隊的一員 , 無論你是企業的一員是你的執行點 , 你的連接器 , 你和他人的能力 , 都能和他人聯絡 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在工業上 , 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的 , 女士們先生們 , 那就是我們和以前從來沒有一模一樣 , 那我們和彼此有著相同的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦已經主導我們國家安全的觀念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前的情況是 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強 , 我很安全 ; 我的聯盟 , 比如北約 , 比他們的聯盟更強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	這已經不是事實了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的出現和相互關聯的出現意味著我與敵人有著相同的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官的時候 , 在1970年代在日內瓦與蘇聯簽約協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和他們有共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方意識到零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著相同的命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	阻礙中東和平的其中一項要素是以色列和巴勒斯坦人都不明白他們有著集體的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 女士們先生們 , 那些曾提起有遠見的人和詩人的年齡層變成我們必須認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 最後會以一首詩結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不用吹響鈴 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每一個人的死都影響著我 , 因為我和人類有關係 , 不要去問鐘聲是什麼人 , 它會為你打滾 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	多恩是道德的建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	我認為 , 對我們而言 , 等式的一部分是生存的 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的道路 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍寶地 」 , 這些長輩與長壽及活躍的社區 , 在tedxtc , 他和九項常見的飲食以及生活習慣 , 保持一百歲以上 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎的研究證實在某些生物限制下人平均壽命只有百分之十是基因所決定的
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其餘的90%是由生活方式決定的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能得到一個實際的公式來維持壽命 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人平均壽命最佳的公式是什麼 , 他們大概不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘的飲食 , 或阿金斯減肥 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國農業部糧食金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是:
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們的是:
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是有很多混淆了真的可以幫助我們活得更久的東西 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	至於營養品 , 你該吃嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或白血球呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	故意在其中演奏嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們該如何社會 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們研究長壽的方法是與國家地理以及國家老化研究所合作 , 來找出四個人口確定地理界線的確認區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後請一群專家加入 , 有條理地通過人們的作為 , 來提煉這些跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我會告訴你們精華是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我要打破一些關於長壽的常見迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是:如果你真的很努力 , 你可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有五千分之一的人能活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的可能性非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	雖然它是美國成長最快的族群 , 但很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們不是為了長壽而設計的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為所謂的繁衍成功 。
i love that word .	我愛這個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學生活
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把這個詞當作成功 , 意思是你有了孩子的年齡 , 接著下一代 , 當你的孩子有了孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	演化的效應完全消失後
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是隻老鼠、大象、或人 , 在這兩者之間 , 都是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以要活到一百歲 , 你不僅要有很好的生活方式 , 你還必須有基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療可以減緩 , 反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	仔細想想 , 總共有99件事情會讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 腦中的氧氣不足 , 腦細胞就會死 , 永遠不會再回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太激烈 , 膝蓋也讓你的軟骨破壞 , 軟骨也再也不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可能會堵塞 , 我們的大腦會用斑塊堵塞 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 上兆個 「 t 」 的部分 , 我們正在討論國家債務號碼 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年一次轉動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每次他們調動就會產生一些傷害 , 傷害就會累積起來 。
and it builds up exponentially .	以指數成長的方式成長 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像過去的日子我們都有披頭四或老鷹的唱片我們會把它加在一個錄音帶上然後讓我們的朋友複製那錄音帶很快地 , 世代代代代相傳聽起來就像垃圾一樣
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有辦法減緩老化或者阻止老化 , 我在這裡幹什麼呢 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上最好的科學告訴我們人類身體 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 已經有90年了 , 對女性來說 , 多了一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家 , 平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在某個時點 , 我們會在飯桌上留下12年美好的光景 。
these are years that we could get .	這些是我們能得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示多年來大部分都免於慢性病心臟病、癌症和糖尿病
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為收到這些消失的最好方法就是看看世界各地的文化 , 那些實際經歷過他們的文化 , 那些地方的人們可以活到一百歲 , 比我們多出十倍 , 那些預期壽命多出十二年 , 中年死亡率只有這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸附近發現了我們的第一個藍色地帶 , 位在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 而是高地 , 一個叫做努奧羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡是男人最長壽 , 大約百歲人瑞的數量 , 比美國多出十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的居民不僅活到一百歲 , 他們還活得很好 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍舊騎腳踏車去工作 , 砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十歲的男人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	牠們的歷史其實可以追溯到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是一個孤立的青銅年代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地非常貧瘠 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 這會出現規律、低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食多以植物為主 , 大多是能被運送到田裡的食物 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做drum小麥 , 這種由草食動物製成的乳酪 , 這種乳酪含高於omega-3脂肪酸而非omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自穀物餵養的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界所知的任何酒都多出三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等大約二十四歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看那些廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在沙丁尼亞 , 你越老越公平 , 你被讚揚的智慧就越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看不到運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不但讓老化的父母跟家人更親近還增加預期壽命四到六年研究顯示對那些家庭有益的孩子也有較低死亡率和較低疾病率的家庭也有益處
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊發現了第二個藍色地帶 , 位在東京的南方 , 位在琉球的阿基戈 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	主島的北端是世界壽命的原點
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這裡發現最老的雌性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有世界上最長的無障礙預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活得很久 , 通常在牠們睡覺時很快就死了 , 我可以告訴你們 , 牠們在做愛後也很快就死了 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	在美國 , 百歲人瑞的人數是五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	結腸癌和乳癌的比率是五分之一 , 在美國這裡是大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這個文化能產生這些數字 , 很明確地表示他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	同樣地 , 植物為主的飲食富含許多顏色的蔬菜
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而他們吃大約八倍的豆腐 , 和美國人一樣 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起吃什麼 , 吃什麼就更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略可以避免過食 , 如你所知 , 在美國有個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們吃飯的盤子比較小 , 所以每次吃的熱量就會比較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其供應家庭風格 , 你可以隨時隨意地吃東西 , 他們在櫃台提供食物 , 然後帶到餐桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一個三千年的格言我認為是有史以來最好的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	它是由孔子所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為是hara、hatchi、bu飲食 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	很簡單 , 這些人在用餐前會說 , 提醒他們不要再吃東西 , 因為他們的胃已經80%飽 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	飽足感要花半小時才能從腹部傳到腦部
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住在80%時休息 , 它能幫助你避免這麼做 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但就像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有少數的社會結構可供延長壽命
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道隔離會導致死亡 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在只有一個半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球你會生在一個自動擁有半打朋友和他們共渡人生的系統
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為模合 。 如果你在模合中 , 碰到運氣好 , 你被期待會分享假如不好 , 孩子生病、父母去世 , 你總會有某個人背對你 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的 「 模合 」 , 這五個女士已經在一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩個部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這指的就是要退出去比較容易的椅子 , 或去亞歷桑那州打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中甚至沒有退休這個字
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 有一個詞會打動你的一生 , 這個詞就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗略的翻譯是 " 早上起床的理由 "
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位一百零二歲的空軍大師來說 , 他的生存價值就是這項武術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 牠一週持續捕魚三次 ,
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是一個問題國家老化研究院確實提供了我們一個問卷給這些百歲人瑞
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們非常有文化觀 , 提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikii是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道他們早上起床的理由 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太來說她的生存價值只是她的曾曾曾孫女
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個年齡在101歲半時分離的女孩 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著一個曾曾曾孫女 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回過頭說: 「 這感覺像是跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我的地理編輯要我去找美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們看了明尼蘇達的草原那裡的百歲人瑞比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但是因為年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的人口 , 屬於前七天的教科生 , 集中在加州的羅馬林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守的衛理師 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝安息日是從星期五日落到星期六日出
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的保護區 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們所遵循的五個小習慣對他們來說是非同尋常的長壽 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的預期壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一個基督復臨派的女人來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更為明顯 , 他們預期平均壽命比美國同伴多11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	出色的研究 , 我覺得它完全描述了這個藍寶地計畫的假設 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個多元的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的是一套生活小習慣 , 終其一生都習慣於儀式性 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中採用他們的飲食
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀第一章第二十九章上帝談到豆子和種子另一節則是談到綠色植物很明顯少了肉
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這間庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不管多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 都要被帶到學校 , 停止一切 , 專注於他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 宗教信仰的天性就是走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	強大之處不在於偶爾能達成它的功用是每週一次能達成一生的
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派教徒往往和其他基督教徒混在一起
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督復臨派的會議 , 你不會看到有人在揮舞吉姆貝姆或正在滾動的會議 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談下一次的自然步行交換食譜 , 當然還有 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但這兩種影響方式極為深遠且明顯 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這種文化讓埃爾斯沃•偉瑞漢出現 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁 , 但當包商想要六千美金來建造隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了這類的錢 , 我自己自己做吧 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天他都在外頭挖掘水泥把北極拖去
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預見的 , 也許到了第四天他被送進了手術室
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上的那個人 , 而是開心手術的那個人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲的他一個月還動二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百零三歲 , 是個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 放棄公雞尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實就住在雙子城這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天都是從舉重開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎她的腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她在1994年的塞維利亞凱迪拉克被感染 , 並在聖貝納迪諾高速公路上流下 , 到現在她仍擔任七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19次困難的探險活動 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你見過的唯一一個人他騎腳踏車橫越撒哈拉沙漠沒有防曬霜
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴你們 , 沒有任何探險比搭馬赫•狄頓的場景更恐怖 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那這三個文化中的共通點是什麼呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	什麼是他們全部都在做的事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們設法歸結成九項 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	實際上 , 我們已經對此進行了兩次藍色探險和這些共同點 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一項我即將要說一項悖論它們都沒有運動至少是我們所認為的運動
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之 , 他們建立起自己的生活 , 使他們不斷地進入物理活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人 , 起身離地面 , 她們坐在地上 , 一天三十到四十次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上下都是 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店、教會、或朋友家都要走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕可以推動 「 院子工作 」 或 「 居家工作 」 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做蛋糕 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	如同跑步機一樣能燃燒卡路里
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	牠們會做有意圖的身體活動 , 這就是牠們喜歡做的事 。 牠們會走路 , 這是唯一證明能消除認知衰退的方法 , 而且牠們都傾向有菜園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式生活 , 才會有正確的人生觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	這些文化每個文化都要花時間下降 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 第七天的教導教徒祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的復原
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你匆匆促或緊張時 , 就會觸發所謂的 「 發炎反應 」 , 這反應和所有疾病有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天減速十五分鐘時 , 你將那發炎狀態轉變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們字彙表達出了目標的意義 , 如同琉球人的本領 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你一生中最危險的兩年就是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及退休那年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的使命感 , 活躍於他們的一生 , 這價值大約是七年的預期壽命
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	取而代之的是 , 這些人每天都會喝一點點東西 , 對於美國人來說也不難賣 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃以植物為基礎的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來避免過食一些小事使他們不受在對的時間點影響
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何建立關係 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和年邁的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全部都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社區 , 一個月就有四到十四次的預期壽命 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	而這裡最重要的是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就遇到對的人就是他們積極地和對的人在一起
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有一半的機率會好轉
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人混在一起 , 隨著時間 , 會有明顯的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友對休閒活動的想法是體力活動 , 保齡球或打曲棍球騎腳踏車或園藝假如你的朋友會喝點東西但吃的不多而且吃得對 , 而且信任又值得信賴那就會隨時間產生最大的影響
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	減肥是行不通的 。 世界歷史上 , 飲食中 , 飲食中曾經超過百分之二的人工作過 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始十月就結束
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	講到長壽並沒有短期的治療 , 不論是藥物或什麼其它的治療 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最重要的事是增加多年的生命和年歲 。 非常謝謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	傳導電流的墨水窗 , 一扇從明確變成不透明的通往切口 ; 一扇能創作音樂的果凍 。 所有東西都存在 , 而catarina說:該是時候來玩 。 mota帶領我們參觀驚喜和酷炫的新材質 , 建議我們將來要做好的實驗 , tker , 擁有娛樂 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	卡塔琳娜•莫塔:利用智慧型材料玩 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機造了一台車 , 讓他能夠運送家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起車子 , 也因為他知道如何蓋車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾幾何時 , 我們了解事物是如何運作的 , 了解它們是如何被製造出來、我們可以建立、修理它們 , 或至少做出有根據的決策來決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多diy資源的做法在20世紀下半葉就被浪費掉了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但 , 現在 , 自造者及開放式資源的模型已經把這些知識 , 帶回到我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個階段 , 由零件所組成 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	通常 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品等傳統材料是由什麼製成 , 以及它們的生產方式 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些奇妙、未來化的複合材料 , 可以改變形狀、可以導電的顏料、會改變顏色的顏料、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電油墨讓我們不用傳統印刷電路或電線來畫電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手中拿著的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來製造一個觸控感應器 , 通過打開這個小光線 , 針對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家早已在用導電油墨 , 但近期發展顯示 , 我們很快就能把它用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這塊丙烯酸纖維附滿了無色的散光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的丙烯酸纖維只會在邊緣散光 , 但當我打開燈時 , 整個表面都會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這類素材的應用包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱變色顏料則會在特定溫度下變色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放到一個火熱板上 , 這裡溫度只比環境高一點點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這項材料主要的應用在嬰兒奶瓶上它能顯示內容物是否涼了可以喝了
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常被稱為智慧型材料的來源 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會被我們每天使用的很多東西和科技所取代 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說裡的飛天車 , 但我們可以有可以依溫度改變顏色的牆壁、鍵盤捲起來的鍵盤、窗戶 , 這些開關變得不透明的了 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 所以 , 為什麼我要來這裡談智能材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對事物的運作感到好奇 , 它們是如何被製造出來的 , 但也因為我相信 , 我們應該要對組成我們世界的元素有更深的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技結合的未來不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以在少量下取得
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資料 , 很少人說它們是如何被製造出來的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們大部分都在商業機密和專利領域中存在 , 只有大學和企業能取得權利 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 我和克絲蒂•波爾開始了一個專案計畫 , 我們稱之為開放式材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	在這個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入的人都可以分享實驗成果 , 發表信息給他人無論何時都可以做出貢獻並收集資源像是其他像我們一樣的自造者的研究報告和輔導
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能變成一個大型、集體生成的數據庫 , 裡面有關於智慧型材料的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要在乎智慧型材料的運作 , 及它們的組成成 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解且使用的東西最後會形塑我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品 , 穿的衣服 , 我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們要活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道且理解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 也同樣重要 , 創新一直都是由改造者推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學很複雜 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家明白這一點他們發表了一篇論文用的是製作導電油墨的方法 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker在讀這篇論文時完全沒有化學經驗 , 他在他的造物空間上進行實驗 , 只靠現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至根據另一個科學家/製造的說明書自製出自己的創投混音器
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登接著在網路上公開了他的結果 , 包括他做了所有嘗試和不成功的事 , 讓其他人可以去研究、重新製作它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬登創新的主要形式就是在設備精密的大學實驗室裡進行一項由設備精密的實驗在芝加哥的車庫裡 , 只用便宜的材料和工具他自己製作的
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人就可以接續下去 , 甚至設計更簡單的處理程序和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提到她的專案的目標是要強調材料的表達性質 , 同時要強調建造者的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝件在教導我們事情的原理 , 是非常強大的 , 但這些限制會影響到我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的辦法是發想出一系列的技術來創造特別的物體 , 讓我們能不受限於設計上的限制 , 來教導我們有關材料本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗裡這是我最喜歡的一項
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有一些銅線 , 連到mp3播放器和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以基於麻省理工學院的研究漢娜將一系列的紙喇叭從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布和油墨等材料中製造出一系列的紙喇叭
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造者漢娜發佈了她的食譜讓任何人都能複製並繁殖它們
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最理想的材料科學領域之一 , 它讓我們能創造出較便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝成品和她分享發現的事實 , 讓門打開一連串美感與創新的新可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	製造者有趣的地方在於我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 而我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不尋常的角度解決問題 , 最後發現其他的 , 甚至更好的方法 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人在材料上實驗 , 越多研究者會願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商也會分享他們的知識 , 我們就有越好的機會創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得我應該有點像泰德尼爾森在1970年代早期寫下 " 你現在應該要了解電腦 "
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是只有科學家在乎的大型主體 , 沒有人想過要在家裡裝一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我站在這裡說 , 有點奇怪 , 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	要記住 , 取得新興科技的先發知識是確保我們有發言權的最佳方式 , 來確保我們能對自己的未來做出發言 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會收到玻璃的氣泡 , 鎖定門和按下加速器 , 靠著我們的眼睛引導我們儘管我們只能看到前後幾個車子 。 但如果車子能和彼此分享資料 , 包括位置和速度 , 以及預測模型 , 用來計算在路上每個人的安全路線 ? 珍妮•海莉想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•喜利:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 宗教圖像和好運的圖標出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而百分之七十五的車禍跟毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	在高速公路上 , 我是個年輕的駕駛 , 而在我面前的車輛 , 我看見煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我心想: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也要慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在高速公路上停車 , 死路 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛剛65歲到0嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs系統啟動了 , 車子還在 , 它不會停止 , 我知道車子不會停 , 空氣袋子開了 , 車子完全安裝了 , 幸運的是 , 沒人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車會停了 , 我想我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛體驗 , 做法是讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我希望各位能想想 , 開車的經驗 , 就是現在的樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上車 。 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃氣泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是在路上 , 以其他大型金屬巨型路面行駛 , 以超人速行駛 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只能用你的眼睛來指導你 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 所以這就是你所有的眼睛 , 這不是設計來完成這個任務的 , 但接著人們要求你做這樣的事 , 你想要換條車道 , 那是他們最先要求你做的嗎 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上移開 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要再看你前進的方向 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 不看你前進的方向 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和所有其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須選擇 , 我們是要看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常 , 我們在路上會做很棒的選擇 , 選擇我們要去哪裡做 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯失某些事物 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會覺得不對或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它要來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看到這麼多的影片 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現今科技的存在 , 可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 如果車輛彼此交換資料 , 我們將能夠看到不只是三輛車前面三輛車 , 在右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 透過觀察鳥眼的視野 , 我們將能看見那些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能夠看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看前面車輛有多快或有多快 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那人要降到零 , 我會知道的 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 不 , 車子不是不可能的
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車是立體的有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	它們沿著道路行走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預期已出版的路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來會變成什麼樣子並不難
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即便如此 , 當你在車子裡 , 有一些摩托車騎士來臨 ! 以時速85英里降下 , 車道我知道你有這種體驗 , 不只是從無中冒出來而已 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上可能已經走了半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10哩前20哩 , 30哩前 , 有人看到那個人 , 一旦一輛車看到那個人 , 並把它放在地圖上 , 他就在地圖上位置 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度繼續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你就會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車也會在他的耳邊小聲說一些話 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 要小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理的預測車的行為
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以開始分享我們車與車之間的位置 , 這樣簡單的事情就是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車子裡有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我就能精準地判斷我在哪裡 , 以及我要飛得多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我就可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 以及他們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以知道他們在哪裡 , 並且大概知道其他車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車子分享資料 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了一個電腦模擬 , 模擬的結果是如何呢 ? 即便是車子可以互相交換 , 當車子可以共用gps資料時 , 我們將這項研究帶離電腦模擬帶到裝有感應器的裝置上 , 用於機器人:立體攝影機、gps , 以及2d雷射檢測設備的位置 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝了一台短距的無線電機 , 讓機器人彼此對話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此碰觸時 , 它們會精準地追蹤對方的位置 , 它們就能避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們在混合當中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你太過聊天 , 要處理所有的封包是很困難的 , 所以你得要把排序做排序 , 預測模型能協助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子都在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你就不會把注意力放在那些組件上 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	首先你要讓這個有點偏離軌道的男人進出前一步 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌道
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他正要偏離航道 , 還知道如何 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪些駕駛員需要提醒自己不要擋路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做的是 , 我們要如何警告大家 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車怎麼輕聲地說: 「 你得趕緊離開嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 取決於兩件事:一 , 車子的性能 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他在手機上 , 或者做些什麼 , 他們可能就無法在緊急狀態中做出最佳的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了分離的研究關於駕駛狀態的模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用三台攝影機來偵測一名駕駛向前看、向下看、透過電話看、喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預知事故我們可以預測是誰車子最好趕出道路給每個人計算最安全的路徑
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 現今的技術是存在的 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我想這是個很讓人不安的概念 , 我們的車會看著我們 , 和其他車子聊天 , 我們將會在八卦的大海中行駛 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信這可以保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我不知道你是誰 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看著你的車牌號碼 , 我不會知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我覺得這將會是件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位花點時間想想 , 如果你真的不想要有那分心的青少年在你背後 , 知道你在煞車 , 知道你要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	通過自願分享數據 , 我們可以為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以讓你的車去管你吧
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	x大獎創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金完成了他的夢想 , 讓他能一起飛上大氣 , 體驗無重力 , 零g的體驗 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	企業、飛行、科學、簡短談話、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的無重力場 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我對打開太空新領域有多麼的熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可思議的 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是基因學的archonxprize 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 要在十天內完成一百個人類基因組測序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有個稱為 「 基因體一百 」 的病人 , 我們的定序為100個 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特會是那事件的主席 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我和霍金教授見面 , 他說他的夢想是上太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你上去 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力變成零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對有 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 唯一能體驗世上無重力飛行的方法 , 其實是有拋物線飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	搭飛機 , 飛到頂部 , 重量為25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	一而再、再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以有8 ~ 10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署訓練太空人太久了 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈將要搭乘史蒂芬•霍金飛機 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們只有一個政府機關 , 和一個公司機關操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你就會殺了這個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的同意 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們開了一場記者會 , 我們宣佈我們打算要做一個無重力拋物面鏡給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切進行得很順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼他會想要這麼做 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他說的對我來說是非常感人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命有不斷增加的風險被災難摧毀......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果不上太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵大眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心在太空總署內的太空飛機位於零號飛機的背面
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	有大約二十個人捐款我們募十五萬美金的兒童慈善機構捐款給那些與我們同行的兒童慈善機構
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾位tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們成立了整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監測他血液的po2、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一我們有緊急情況發生時的一切 ; 天知道 , 你不想要傷害這位世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭起降的地方 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴byronlichtenberg小心翼翼地將他處於零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他抵達 , 我們就會讓他去體驗無重力的真正感覺 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物線飛行傘之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在笑 , 我們說: 「 開始吧 。 」
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的為艾薩克•牛頓致敬 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋大學擔任相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四、第五、第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	還有第七和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他很高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們是活在一個珍貴的珠寶裡而這是我們一生都在離我們而去的
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這趟壯舉之旅 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫用動畫-大衛•布林斯基出現了3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 呈現出一個細胞內的忙碌生活 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、藥物、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛波林斯基對一個細胞進行動畫 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是一位醫學繪圖師 , 我的觀點有點不同 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以後 , 我就一直在觀察著藝術、真與美的表現 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	儘管這些都是他們自身的美好事物 , 他們都有美妙的事物 , 能讓他們知道真與美 , 能被科學及數學視為理想的雙胞胎 , 就像是科學家想要約會的理想雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是所謂的 「 真相 」 的表現 , 敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是很理想的 , 不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時很有用 , 通常是很久之後才會發現的 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在就可以開始播放一些照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	對不懂科學的人來說 , 真與美常常都不太樂觀 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們描述了美 , 常常只有在你了解人類所使用的語言和語法中 , 研究哪種真與美的人才會使用的語言 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看看宇宙的常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 從描述宇宙的數字中 , 可以發現生命演化出了這些真的很難理解的東西 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	我嘗試做的是自從我被醫學插圖師教導我的動畫是一位雕塑家和視覺導師我希望能找到方法幫助人們理解生物科學中的真與美以用動畫、照片來說故事讓人們聽得更清楚因此人們不見得能被帶到的東西可以被教導、可以被教導
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生常常沉浸在一種環境中 , 他們所學習到的 , 是有真與美的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是分類式化的 , 這點被吸引的 , 不見得都是事實和美麗的主題 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就好像原始雞湯的食譜 , 烹煮雞肉直到香味消失為止 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣對學生做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真的開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子和細胞生物學系的robertlue打來的電話 。 他問我我跟我的團隊有沒有興趣 , 願意改變哈佛醫學和科學教育的做法 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的專案 , 這個計劃能探討分子和細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 學生能夠了解所有這些事實背後的更大圖像 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們腦海中可能會有個細胞的影像 , 那個城市是一片繁忙、非常複雜的大城市 , 由微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械確實位於生命的中心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 能讓全世界的奈米工程師嫉妒 , 它們是能自我引導、強大、精確、精準的裝置 , 由氨基酸鏈所組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械讓細胞移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動細胞複製 , 驅動我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們能影響我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	因此我們想做的是將這個故事製作成一個動畫這會是哈佛大學bivisionsions的主角這是個哈佛大學為它的分子和細胞生物學生所做的研究除了所有的文字資料外外這些學生將有視覺化的視覺化的視覺化的學生對這些細胞的真實面貌和美麗的研究能夠在他們的心中深處發揮他們的想像力所以這些研究的過程會是他們對生命的熱誠和意味所以他們能夠發揮他們的想像力所以他們能夠發現生命能夠發現生命的新觀點
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子的排列狀況 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們想出了一個大主題就是巨噬細胞正在沿著微血管細胞的表面流下 , 它們會接觸到微血管壁的表面 , 它們會收集在微血管壁上的細胞資訊 , 它們會收集到室外發炎的資訊 , 讓他們看不見和感官的資訊 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓它們停止 , 會讓他們內化 , 他們需要做出各式各樣的零件 , 來改變它們的形狀 , 試圖從微血管中找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛的科學家一起研究 , 研究原子上精確的分子模型 , 並弄清楚它們是如何移動的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	並且找出方法來實現這一點 , 一個準確的事實 , 即它公開了正在發生的一切 , 但事實並非如此 。 一個細胞內非常緊密的群眾會阻止這個視野復甦 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要讓大家看一段我們製作的第一部份 , 三分鐘的讀者消化版 。 這是一個持續進行的專案計畫 , 會延續四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這一點 , 看到細胞製造的路徑這些會走動的小型機器 , 它們是驅動蛋白 , 負責大量使用 , 大量使用相對大小的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動著細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同狀況的細胞內發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會利用讀取基因的分子從細胞核中取出的零件 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 如果沒有這些微機械 , 就有可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率真的會很低 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞中的fedex快遞人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 拉一個包裹著全新的蛋白質到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜 , 不論是到達器官 , 不論是用來製造或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	而我們每個人體內都有大約10萬個這種分子在運作 , 就在現在 , 每一百兆個細胞裡 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上 , 你並沒有在做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家之後 , 我要你想想這一點 , 並想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們學到的關於細胞機械的一些東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了一切 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道發生了什麼事 , 只要我們搞清楚發生了什麼事 , 我們就能真正地能夠掌控我們對健康的掌控 , 掌握我們對未來世代的操作 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們可以藉此發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很不可思議 , 它們足以察覺細胞的需要它們是如何運作的 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們合作 。 它們使細胞能做到它所需要的 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們的合作協助我們身體一個巨大的實體 , 它們永遠不會看到正常的實體 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	請繼續欣賞接下來的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	beckyblanton打算在她的車上住一年 , 看看這個國家 , 但是當經濟蕭條和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營工作變成了無家可歸的旅程 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國工作無家可歸的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生命、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:那一年我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是個極端好奇的人 , 所以 , 在新聞工作22年間 , 我學會了很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事就是變成隱形的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年2月去世之後我決定旅行
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死很重擊我 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當時我在做這件事的時候 , 我想要感受並處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 , 我決定住在旅行車裡一整年的生活就像一趟漫長的露營旅程 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了我的貓 , 我的洛威爾和我的露營裝備 , 轉到1975年的雪佛蘭 , 然後開車去日落 , 完全沒想到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:社會把價值當作一個永恆的結構 , 甚至一個小屋 , 視為一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到 , 很快地 , 其他人的負面看法會影響我們的現實 , 只要我們願意的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡、定期吃東西 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間休息和哀悼悲痛 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親死去的憤怒和沮喪出現了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我自由工作結束了 , 我得要有全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來溫和的春天變成極度炎熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到處都看不見我有一隻貓跟狗 , 牠真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓從車窗出來 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	整天都在照顧狗狗 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我可以在辦公大樓裡 , 我都會用淋浴頭和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公眾洗手間洗身 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下卻無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在高溫下腐壞
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰箱幾小時之內就融化了 , 當時的情況非常悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法找到一間公寓 , 或買不起一間公寓 , 能讓我有腐爛的公寓和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄 , 所以我待在旅行車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當夜間的高溫讓我連走50英尺到公共洗手間時 , 我也常用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度在冰點以下的狀態下降 。 他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面臨全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	每晚我都停車去一個不同的地方 , 這樣我就不會被注意到 , 被警察困擾 。
i didn't always succeed .	我不是每次都成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得我無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時、何地發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家、記者 , 變成了無家可歸的小車 , 被帶走了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒變 , 我的智商沒降
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天賦、我的誠信、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的一切都是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我有些改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪的旋轉中更深入、更深 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終 , 有人提醒我要去一間流浪漢健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊中人一樣沮喪和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我就是不喝醉 , 不論高醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當一些無家者發現包括一位前任大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的人 , 你為什麼還在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者不認為我是無家者 , 但我還是認為我是無家可歸者 ,
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	那位教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你抱有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的憂鬱症 , 讓我有自殺傾向 , 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我自殺 , 就不會有人注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一個朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯 , 一個知名記者 , 在全國電視上談到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我曾寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前一年 , 關於提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	當時他在做我的寫作電路 。 他在談論我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我發現提姆•羅斯 , 《與媒體見面》的前主持人 , 正在談論我的寫作 , 那時我還住在一輛在沃爾瑪的停車場的旅行車 , 我開始大笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了 , 因為接近了我的家 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的婦女 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 。 我重新讀了我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後 , 我搬回了田納西州 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車中間 , 和沙發衝浪 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的夏天 , 我是個記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我是個得獎者 。 我住在我自己的公寓 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數千人全職、兼職工作 , 住在車上 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但是社會持續汙名化和犯罪化──住在車上或在街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家者、工作無家者 , 大多還是不被看見 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們 , 參與他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服一切事物 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我來這裡並不是代表流浪漢的代表 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們捐錢給下一位乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在他們住的地方 , 他們在哪裡睡覺 , 他們在任何時間的狀態下的生活狀態 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在旅行車裡的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是能找到一條路 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxange , thailand的 " 保險套 " 中 , schaivivaidya , 帶領我們走遍全國的大膽計劃 , 提升其生活水準 , 從七零年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著有很多frank , 開玩笑也非常有效的關於保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	密西西比亞:保險套讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常、非常的窮 , 有許多許多的人民生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定對此採取一些行動 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或從貧窮減少計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃計畫開始 , 接下來是非常成功的母子健康活動 , 成群的活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 如果他們的孩子無法生存 , 根本沒有人會接受節育計畫 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:先找孩子 , 找媽媽 , 然後再跟著做家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩童死亡率 , 還需要節育計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧看看為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的事 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭平均有7個小孩 , 人口成長率是極高的3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女性說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 而且我們只有非常少數的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不把答案當作答案 , 而是以一個問題來看待這個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找同樣是婦女的護士和助產士 , 在解釋使用藥丸時做得非常好 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但那只覆蓋了全國20%的人口 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們給另外80%的人做的是讓他們獨自一人然後說: 「 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去看了你看到的平凡人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色標牌底下--我希望他們還沒被拿走 , 因為那裡有 " 可口可樂 " 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們所選的人 , 是我們所選擇的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道客戶永遠是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己會做節育計畫 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國每一個村落裡提供避孕藥和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以我們去了 。 我們去了那些被視為是問題的根源 , 成為解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論人們在哪裡 , 你都能看到船上有婦女 , 賣的是水上市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找到人 , 你都能在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是那個藍色的 , 不是那個黃色的 , 拿著一碗聖水給僧人 , 把聖水灑在藥丸和保險套上 , 為了家人的聖潔 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片到處流傳全國 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧侶自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	婦女說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	結果是受到祝福的 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	接著我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每一個人去試著提供任何能讓人類成為更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導如何用新的字母來規劃家庭規劃--a是出生、b是保險套、i是子宮頸切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有一個蛇和梯子的比賽 , 你跳骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落在任何該有的規劃上 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是: 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	很好 , 媽媽 , 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 。 很好 , 叔叔 。 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	舅舅喝醉了 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 又重新開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育和娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有接力賽 , 我們有兒童的保險套 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	過不久 , 保險套就成了女孩的好朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人而言 , 鑽石並不會讓安全套成為女孩的好朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年提出了第一個小額貸款計劃 , 婦女組織說: 「 我們只想借錢給那些實施家庭規劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
