the text here is right side and upside down so that you are forced to turn the book around , and you can see it from ground point of view and from her point of view looking in the hole , getting a different kind of perspective , moving you around the space . particularly appropriate in a building that can contain perfectly a sphere dimensions of the diameter being the same as the distance from the center of the floor to the center of the oculus .	這裡的文字是對的 , 上下顛倒過來 , 所以你被迫轉書本 , 從地面角度看 , 從她的角度去看 , 從地面上看 , 從地面向上看 , 以不同類角度看 , 繞著你轉 。 尤其是適當的建築物 , 直徑是和地表的中央直徑是完全相同的 。
unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	不幸的是 , 這條線纏住了一些正在參觀萬神殿的男孩們 , 他們立刻被拉出來 , 進行一段非同尋常卻又驚人的巡迴表演 , 從他們的角度來看 , 很自然的從他們的角度上就上下了 。
they bail out as soon as they get to the top of saint ivo , that little spiral structure you see there .	保釋一旦抵達聖伊沃峰頂 , 你就會看到那個螺旋狀的結構 。
she continues on her way over piazza navona .	她繼續前往那佛那廣場 。
notices a lot of activity at the tre scalini restaurant , is reminded that it is lunchtime and she's hungry .	在trespalini餐廳看到很多活動提醒她現在午餐時間很餓
they keep on motoring towards the campo de' fiori , which they soon reach . ajax the dog is put in a basket and lowered with a list of food into the marketplace , which flourishes there until about one in the afternoon , and then is completely removed and doesn't appear again until six or seven the following morning .	牠們會繼續朝鮮花廣場行駛很快就到了 。 小狗阿賈克斯會被放在籃子裡 , 把一份食品列入市場 , 開到下午一點 , 才會完全被丟棄 , 直到隔天六、七點才會出現 。
anyway , the pooch gets back to the dirigible with the stuff .	總之 , 小狗回到了飛船 。
unfortunately , when she goes to unwrap the prosciutto , ajax makes a lunge for it .	不幸的是 , 當她去解開這支針筒時 , 阿賈克斯吃了一頓午餐 。
she's managed to save the prosciutto , but in the process she loses the tablecloth , which you can see flying away in the upper lefthand corner .	她成功救了這條桌布 , 但在過程中 , 她失去了桌布 , 這條桌布就可以看到在左上角飛走 。
they continue without their tablecloth , looking for a place to land this thing so that they can actually have lunch .	他們沒有桌布 , 想找個地方降落 , 這樣他們就可以吃午餐 。
they eventually discover a huge wall that's filled with small holes , ideal for docking a dirigible because you've got a place to tie up .	他們最終發現了一堵巨牆 , 裡面都是小洞 , 用來做防禦用途是理想的 , 因為你有地方可以連結在一起 。
turns out to be the exterior wall that part of it that remains of the coliseum , so they park themselves there and have a terrific lunch and have a spectacular view .	結果發現那面牆是羅馬殘留下來的外牆 , 所以他們停在那裡 , 吃很棒的午餐 , 景色壯觀 。
at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	吃完午餐後 , 他們又開了一會兒 , 來到卡拉的浴場 , 來到城裡的牆上 , 然後一個廢棄的大門 , 決定再看一眼賽斯提烏斯金字塔 , 上面有條閃電線 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 問題來了:他們有點太靠近 , 而當你在飛船上時 , 你得要非常小心尖刺 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	這讓她的故事得以總結 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , 馬爾切洛有點懶惰 , 但他中午才下班 。
so , the alarm goes off and it's five to 12 or so .	所以 , 鬧鐘響了 , 大概5 ~ 12次 。
he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 躍上他的腳踏車 , 橫越城市 , 聖母里亞•德拉的教堂 , 穿過小巷 , 穿過街道 , 觀光客可能隨時都在穿越 , 打破羅馬的安靜生活 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	那個他正在移動的速度 , 我希望我已經建議到這個小圖像 , 同樣地 , 也可以從兩側翻轉 , 因為下面有簡訊 , 上面的字是上下顛倒的圖像 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續前進 , 接近一間毫不知情的服務生 , 試圖在精緻的白葡萄酒蚌醬裡提供兩塊多餘的語言 , 給坐在街上餐廳外的客人吃 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務員很緊張 , 但已經太遲了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	馬爾切洛還在他的踏板上前進 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	從這一刻起 , 他看到的所有東西都有點受語言的影響 , 但仍然繼續前進 , 因為這個人有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去了一些支架 。 羅馬仍是個不可思議的地方 , 是因為支架和決心要維持結構 , 羅馬繼續成長 , 適應特定時間的需求 , 否則我們會發現它 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	就在廣場 「 德拉•羅通達 」 一路走到萬神殿前 , 又一次的令人心碎 , 最終終於成功了 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , 馬爾切洛是64輛巴士的司機 。 如果你坐過64輛巴士 , 你知道巴士開得跟馬塞羅在他的摩托車上展示的一樣 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	終於carletto , 你可以看到他在左上角的公寓
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他正盯著桌子看 ; 今晚他打算向他的女友求婚40年 , 他希望一切都完美 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他有蠟燭 , 中間有花朵 , 他正在想著該把杯盤和杯子放在哪裡 。
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他不快樂 , 不對勁 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	電話響了 , 他被叫去palazzo 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他在一個好的短片之中不斷反擊 , 比起我們剛剛看到的那些旅行 , 他簡直嚇人了 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道carletto , 因為他在娛樂界 , 其實他在電視界 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	事實上他在電視修復方面 , 這也是人們認識他的原因 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的電話號碼 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他到達了廣場 , 抵達大門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	走進院子 , 和看門人聊天 , 醫生告訴他 , 宮殿裡發生了一場災難 ; 沒有人在電視上工作 , 即將有一場足球大賽 , 人群越來越不安 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他下到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後慢慢地爬到樓頂 , 每間公寓都在檢查 , 檢查每一間電視機 , 想找出問題的所在 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他一直往上爬 , 終於到了大樓的樓梯 , 一個小樓梯直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一張桌布掛在房子裡的電視天線上 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他除去它 , 問題就解決了 , 宮殿中的所有人都很快樂 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決了自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在要做的就是用一張完美的桌子 , 等著她抵達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎沒有很大的意義去傳達我想要表達的關於羅馬的訊息 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我就先畫廣場 , 然後我會進進去和下面 , 向下展示這些東西 , 並且展示它們的形成方式等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我只拿我最喜歡的位元和碎片 , 把它們放到萬神殿裡 , 保持原有的尺寸 , 這樣你就可以看到聖誕節的頂端 , 還有賽斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 還有布拉曼特的陽台 , 都在這一邊 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這只是一張圖 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮拉內西來見埃斯契爾 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我已經開始真正地失去控制 , 同時也希望了 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍色線條 , 貫穿了這些線 , 讓它們維繫在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不光是收集和儲存信息的便捷方法 , 它也是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我是說 , 你總是把一層一層的剝開 ; 我們認為他們是一頁 , 以某種特定的方式來處理 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成各層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個有層次地層次的地方 , 垂直地層次 。 我想 , 如果剝開一個頁面 , 可以讓我用正確的方式來思考 , 讓我呈現出各層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大樓的泥土牆上覆蓋了許多疤痕 ; 數世紀來的疤痕隨著這些建築物不斷改變 , 而不是被拆除 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左邊畫一個摺疊頁 , 讓你展開它 , 你將看到一個疤痕組織的背後 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製造出更小的窗戶是非常必要的 , 因為壞人要來了 , 諸如此類 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	各式各樣的適應作用都埋在了之底 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以將一頁的涵蓋掉 , 讓你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也可以告訴各位 , 在那些雄偉建築的角落中 , 那些巨大的石塊 , 或用磚塊做成的假石塊 , 和粘土比較常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它有點立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你走下一條狹小的街道 , 進入一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 使用雙扇摺疊處 , 雙扇摺疊頁 , 如果你和我小時候一樣 , 正在讀一本書 , 希望你將你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你頭上的紙張都裹在廣場中 , 留給那個短暫的時間 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我實在沒有做任何更複雜的摺疊頁 ,
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	我們來看看萬神殿和前面的羅通達廣場
here's a book completely wide open .	這本書完全打開了 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	如果我不打開書 , 如果我只打開九十度 , 我們就在盯著萬神廟的正面看 , 我們在上面往下看 , 大概就是往下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書換個角度 , 我們就在萬神殿的正面看著廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有把戲--只有一本沒有打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我想 , 也許我可以在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺疊文字和唯一開放的書結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	我們進入萬神殿內部 , 它會不斷地成長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我正走對路 , 但它似乎已經失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 它總是一件好事 , 如果你想要引起人們注意 , 注意讀書並在過程中取得資訊 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進展 」 震撼了我 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果這是一隻寄生鴿 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果標題行得通 , 用它 。 但它會是一趟穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示了我喜歡羅馬的一切 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	它是教堂頂上的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天飛走 , 做鴿子該做的事 , 回來了 , 整個地方都被鷹架和綠色網路覆蓋而且這隻鴿子不可能回家了
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以這是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找另一個棲息地 , 這使我能在我喜愛的目錄中找到另一個棲息地 。 我們從較高的棲息地開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回家和家人住在一起 ; 這不一定是好事 , 但會讓鴿子再次結合在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這很有趣 , 但或許有一個人需要以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以 , 我想到了這個老傢伙一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方讓他們變得危險的地方 , 他們和這個人成了朋友 , 學會了在午餐時間表演技巧 , 像這樣的地方來娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	這種老人和這些鴿子之間的真實連結正逐漸形成 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 , 病的很嚴重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 即aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在一個三四天沒見到他之後就出現了 。 他住在一個小閣樓裡 , 然後他們把他的名字轉來轉去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 像是紅氣球 , 都在等著他 , 然後他們把他帶走 , 帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘記了這件事:只要他失去一隻鴿子 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城市外的牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的古老習俗 , 去世的人從來沒有被埋在牆壁中 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這個故事真的很令人開心 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這將會有很長的路要走 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了一次又一次的 , 如果包裝不成功 , 如果故事不會到哪裡去 , 我會設立標題 , 希望書名會朝正確的方向把我趕下 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它真的讓我有足夠的專注 , 我甚至會做個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	這些全是書標題 , 最終引領我找到解答 , 這是關於一位年輕女子的故事 , 她用一種回敬的鴿子寄一封信給她住在羅馬城外的一個人 , 送到城市裡的某個人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子就在阿基安的上方飛來飛去
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看見墳墓、松果等等 ,
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你看到的是鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它已經變成必要且可行了 , 試圖傳達出那種在城市中飛行的感覺 , 且不用動彈 。

this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大多數鴿子不做的事:它選擇了一條景象路線 , 我覺得這個裝置是必須把這本書延伸到四頁以外的地方 。

we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和palazzofarnese相撞 , 由米開朗基羅設計 , 用從羅馬競技場延伸出的石頭建成 。

this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這完全是防守化的 , 不允許任何規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的透視法就是 , 看起來是可信的 , 你成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你要試著知道哪些地方會消失 ; 火星上和別的部分則在克雷莫納 。

now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這張圖表明被足球撞擊的畫面很糟 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:聖母堂 , 和平聖母堂 , 有足球 , 有一點點鳥的翅膀 , 什麼都沒有發生 , 所以我得要重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	假如你真的想看到聖母瑪莉亞•德拉的步調 , 這些書非常靈活 , 非常有互動性 , 就這樣轉過身去 , 用另一種角度去看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到效果被標記在紅線上 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥類能自行拉過這座中世紀的高塔 , 剩下的中世紀建築塔之一 , 前往聖地納堂的教堂附近 , 往下看 , 帕雅扎納已經提過、看過、飛了好幾次 ; 有著伯尼的四條河雕像 , 然後經過好美妙的博羅米諾齊聖安諾大道 , 停在我們靠近的26英尺高的地方 , 萬萬萬萬萬神殿直徑 , 來吸引人 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	這樣我們可以在室內盤旋 , 因為我們在飛 , 我們就不用再擔心重力了 , 所以這幅圖可以隨時隨地擺動 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	飛過耶和華的時候 , 我們有一點精彩 ; 用這種方式來模仿這個建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過去我所提到的 " 混合點 " 牆上充滿了完美的牆壁 ; 美麗的雕刻場佈滿了neon 「 暴風者號 」 標誌 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們終於抵達了palazzo的庭院 , 也就是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一扇小窗戶 , 到閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿上除去訊息 ; 上面這麼寫道 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著設計圖的板子時 , 我們看到他正在做的事情 , 事實上 , 是鴿子設計的地圖 , 紅線會貫穿所有景象 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要那些資訊 , 所以我們完成了這個理解的循環 , 你所要做的就是讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的摩天兔子研究自行組合這個想法:與其建造一些東西 , 我們可以創造出能自己的東西 , 將dna鏈接合起來的方式 , 這是一個很大的概念 。 蒂比斯向我們展現了三項自組裝未來的計劃 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	高空的tibbit:我們能否做出他們自己的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向你們展示我們未來製造東西的方法 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築物和機器很快就會變成自我組合、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要告訴你們我相信目前的製造方式 , 然後把它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 50萬至一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜、嶄新、令人振奮的鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器可以帶領我們進入太空-250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒中摺疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然生態系統有著這種複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建立的東西都更有效率 , 遠超過任何我們可以建造的任何東西都還要複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	牠們也能修復自己長壽
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然生態系統有一個超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把這個概念轉換成我們的建築環境 , 那就有一些令人興奮的潛力在我們建造東西的過程中 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想利用我們在實體環境裡的自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的複雜性 , 這樣我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列--基本上就是我們建築物的運作方式的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以採用該序列來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源 , 讓它能夠活化 , 讓我們的部分能夠折疊計劃 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的矯正措施來保證我們已經成功地實現自己想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我將向你們展示一些項目 , 是我和麻省理工學院同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些項目都是大規模的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們與機電設備、感測器嵌入 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要解碼什麼 , 可以折疊成一連串的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--諸如此類 。 一連串的角度 , 或轉彎 , 然後你就將序列通過弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都需要它的消息--負120--它是旋轉的 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師參與這個項目的設計師 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的能讓我們明白:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 數個小時創造了8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能不能真正擴大規模 ? 我們能不能真正嵌入機器人到每個部分 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 關注的是被動天性 , 或被動地嘗試重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它又更進一步 , 嘗試實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上包含了最根本的計算 , 數位邏輯 , 直接進入你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是個nand邏輯閘口 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個正四面體是門 , 它會做你的計算 , 而你有兩個輸入的正四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是來自使用者的輸入 , 一旦你蓋好了你的磚 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從以前被放置的磚 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它可以讓你在三維空間中輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著用戶可以開始連接他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它以前的行為 , 你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 數字會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 就會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們擁有所有內建的資料
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這種情況下 , 我稱之為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構包含著確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以換個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部嵌入的信息會告訴你如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有攀登的東西 , 讀取它 , 然後在一開始輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將要展示的最後一個項目叫做偏頗鏈 , 它可能是我們現在被動自組裝系統最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它將可重組性和可編程性 , 並使它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一個元素鏈 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都完全相同 , 而且它們偏頗 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	每一條鏈、每一個元素 , 都想要向右或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈的時候 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每一個單位是否應該向右轉或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以 , 當你搖動鏈條時 , 它會摺疊成任何你編程的配置--在這種情況下 , 一個螺旋 , 或這個例子 , 是兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以設計任何立體形狀或單一維度的二維向上進入這條通道完全被動地
so what does this tell us about the future ?	這告訴我們什麼關於未來的信息呢 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想這告訴我們 , 在我們的物理結構、建築物、機器中 , 有新的自組裝、複製、修復的可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些地區有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有磚塊都能計算出來 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的並行以及分散的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我給你們展示的這些項目 , 只是對未來的一小步 , 如果我們實施這些新技術 , 讓它成為一個全新的自組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸地圖 , 我們甚至去過海底的最深點 。 下一代還留給了什麼探索 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe提到這個答案:幾乎所有 。 然後我們可以開始 , 他說:與那些不可思議、小到的世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學 ,
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼要探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡表揚一位偉大的20世紀探險家羅伊•查普曼安德魯斯
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	安德魯斯在美國自然歷史博物館 , 帶領一系列的考察隊伍 , 前往未知的區域 , 像是這裏 , 戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個不錯的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說 , 他後來成為印第安那瓊斯這個角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我給一群中學生公開演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡告訴各位 , 如果有比ted這裡演講更嚇人的話 , 它會試著將一千個12歲的人的注意力集中在45分鐘的演講中 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講的最後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那之後 , 還有一個問題困在我身上 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們要去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想有很多人覺得地球的探索年代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們會去外太空或深海的地方 , 去找重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有其他地方可以讓我們探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想到生物史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始發現菸草鑲嵌疾病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他做的是從菸草植物中取出受感染的汁液 , 然後用越來越小的過濾器來過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	到達某個程度他覺得一定有什麼東西比當時已知的細菌最小的生命形式還要更小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他神秘的媒介命了名 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 拉丁文
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的同時 , beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	現在我們知道 , 病毒構成了地球上絕大部分的基因信息 , 遠超過所有其他形式的生命體的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然已經有大量的實用應用和這個世界有關係--比如消滅天花 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒所引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們已經有了汽車 , 但我們還沒有意識到我們星球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有驚人的工具 , 讓我們能探索未知的世界--像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做的不僅僅是表面 , 還能觀察特定物種的個別基因組 , 還能觀察整個宏觀的群體 , 我們身邊充滿微生物的群落 , 記錄這些種類中所有的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚之間的所有東西上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們定期處理這種疫情的成因 , 來確認疫情的成因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓你們對它的運作方式有概念 , 想像一下 , 我們取出你們每個人的鼻腔腫瘤 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會去尋找呼吸道疾病的病毒 , 像是流行性感冒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些遺傳信息 , 當然 , 我們會看到一些普通的嫌疑犯 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 主要是來自你鼻子內完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了令人非常驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡大約有20%的基因信息並不符合任何我們以前見過的東西 , 不論是植物、動物、真菌、細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們研究這種資料的小小團體 , 其實我們當中有些人開始稱之為 「 資訊生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何我們以前見過的東西 ; 它有點像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多東西 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子中20%的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	甚至在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的信息是暗物質無法被分類或配對任何我們看到的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這也許是人工製品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度排序的技術還相當新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著他們愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定信息是生命的一種形式 , 至少其中的一些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設還在初期階段 , 有非常令人振奮的可能性存在:那就是埋在生命裡的 , 遺傳信息是還未被辨識出的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c和g , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命類型 , 像beijerinck , 它會從根本改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	那或許能讓我們找出折磨我們的癌症的原因 , 或是找出我們不熟悉的爆發來源 , 或可能在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣佈 , 和在史丹佛、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事一起 , 我們正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 以尋求新生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們還沒有意識到病毒 , 這種生命形式就是我們星球上大部分基因信息的生物 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚訝 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到一種新的生命類別 , 都在我們的眼睛底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物但這並不表示地球上沒有其它可探索的事物
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同類提供了重要的啟示給下一代來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的探險家 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	如果我們要引用這堂課的話 , 應該是這樣的:不要假設我們現在認為已經有了完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求任何一個你選擇去探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們四周都有未知的事物 , 只等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch把理論的物理理論放在保守角落 , 來討論更緊急的問題:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、宇宙、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•狄特森在我們在宇宙中的位置 ,
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要出去並說些驚人的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事說起 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一項 , 事實上是有史以來被記錄下來的東西 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是 , 地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境等等 , 都是獨一無二的適合人類演化或創造 , 因為我們過去認為和現在存在 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	如今這個想法有個戲劇化的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這想法就是在太空船之外宇宙不可調和的對人類有敵意而且內部是我們賴以生存的
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有別的進展了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都知道的是 , 和人類歷史上大部份人所相信的相反 , 人類其實不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如同斯蒂芬•霍金說過的 , 我們只是普通行星表面的化學污垢 , 圍繞著典型的恆星運行 , 位在一個典型的銀河系的邊緣 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	第一個大家都知道的事是說我們正處於一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合等等 。 第二個則是說我們正處於一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你將這兩項真相視為人生中的深層真相 , 並告知你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎會互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們兩者都是完全錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	這些是的 。 讓我從第二個故事開始:典型的 , 這是典型的場所嗎 ? 讓我們看看四周 , 隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污染物 , 這一點都不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只要朝同一個方向走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你看不到任何牆或化學污垢 。 如果你更進一步看 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系 , 和恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為恆星是銀河系的 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部份地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 都不在任何一個星系附近 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以讓我們繼續往外看 , 直到我們超越了銀河系 , 然後再往回看 , 那裡有一個巨大的星系 , 螺旋武器擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	到目前為止 , 我們已經從這兒移到十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們離宇宙中典型的地方還很遠 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達典型的 「 星系間空間 」 , 就要到一千倍以上 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那到底是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	以極大的代價 , ted排列出一個高解析度的模擬實境虛擬的星際空間 , 從星系間的空間來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 看得見嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不盡然 , 在星系間空間中 , 星系間空間是完全黑暗的 , 漆黑一片 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	黑暗到如果你正看著離你最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星爆炸成了超新星 , 當光線抵達時 , 你要直視它 , 甚至連光線都看不到 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是如此的巨大、黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管事實上 , 超新星是如此的明亮 , 如此的聰明 , 它會在多個光年中殺死你 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你根本看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷 , 溫度低於絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	這真空的 。 真空的密度是地球上最好的科技所能創造的密度的一百萬倍 。 這就是一個典型的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能不能把燈光打回上面 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	目前我們對一個如此遙遠、如此不同、如此陌生的環境所知 , 和我們習以為常的環境相差甚遠 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球──我們的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 創造了知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那是什麼意思呢 ? 看看遠比我們剛才所說的更遠 , 有了望遠鏡你會看到像星星的東西
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 類星體 」 , 原始的意思是類星體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	也就是說 , 看上去有點像星星 。 但不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 一個星系中心的物質朝著超大質量黑洞瓦解 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 密集的磁場引導了那重力崩潰的一些能量 。 還有一些物質 , 形成了極大的風暴 , 照亮了葉子的光輝 , 我認為那是萬億個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	此時 , 人腦的物理根本不會像噴射機一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在那瞬間存活下來 。 一旦試圖描述這種風暴的情形 , 語言就會崩潰 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但是是在極端的範圍 , 以及每次經歷數百萬年的變化 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這個噴射流發生得如此精準 , 以至於數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 一些化學污垢可以精確地描述和模型 , 和預測 , 和解釋 , 最重要的是 , 在現實中 , 你的感受到到到的現象 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個類星體的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不只是膚淺的圖像 , 雖然也包含這個圖像 , 還包含解釋性的模型 , 具體呈現相同的數學關係和因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠神奇 , 一個結構相似 , 另一種的信念就會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這個實體物體 , 儘可能彼此不同 , 但卻仍然可以體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間 , 越來越多的實體結構 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一種與眾不同的化學污垢 。 這種化學污垢有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著不斷的精準度 , 一切的結構 。 這個地方 , 而非宇宙的其它地方 , 是包含在內的一個中心 , 包含在它所有物理實相的結構和因果關係中 。 所以 , 它的物理定律不能被微不足道德 , 甚至可以被授予 , 是對物理世界來說最重要的事物的重要事物之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和環境是如何形成的呢 ? 以我們人類與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金的評論中 , 有一點是正確的 , 但那是錯誤的強調 。 有一點是正確的 。 它沒有任何特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的放寬沒有奇蹟的存在 。 它有三個我們所擁有的充足範圍 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 信息處理就是計算計算計算 , 電腦需要有一台電腦 , 完全不知道如何讓電腦產生出沒有物質的電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們還需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 較不容易實現 , 但對於開放式的知識和解釋 , 也有同樣重要的關鍵 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境中充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好做了測試比如 , 牛頓的地心引力定律大約在三百年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但 , 我們過去做過的證據 , 在幾十億年前 , 地球上每一平方公尺上都不斷墜落 , 之後還會持續數十億年 。 其他科學也一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學中最根本的真相的證據 , 就在這裡佔據我們的星球 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們所在的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件就在它們的供應鏈中 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 那裡是空的 ; 那裡是冷的 ; 還是漆黑的 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實這只是另一個狹義的誤解
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	試想在星系間空間中的立方體 , 和我們的房子大小一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 立方體的空地是人類的標準 , 但那也意味著 , 它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠建造一座自給自足的太空站 , 一群科學家致力於創建開放式的知識流 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成其他元素等等都遠不夠 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題是 , 在一個可以理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麽 , 除了知道如何之外 , 還有什麼可以阻止我們去做呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣地 , 如果我們能自動獲得能源供應 , 因為變遷會是核融合反應爐和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再次強調 , 這對人類的感官很黑暗 。 但你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是用現今的設計 , 看看外面 , 和我們看到的銀河系一樣 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	用一個更強大的望遠鏡就能看到星星和行星
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 學習物理的定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	定位在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習初級粒子物理學 , 化學 , 等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	也許最難做的科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為要花數百萬年才能到達最近的有生命的星球 , 再返回地球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , 理查--但我從來不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔幾億年就盡一己之力 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以 , 事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含所有開放式知識的前提 。 任何這類的立方體 , 都可以變成和我們一樣的樞紐 , 如果知道如何進行的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並沒有處在一個特別適合居住的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果銀河系間的空間能夠創造出一串開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都是如此 。 地球也是 。 污染的地球也是如此 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 就在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充足 , 但知識是稀少的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙知識為基礎的觀點也許--我認為這應該會讓我們感到很特別--但也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著如果沒有這種具體的知識能在宇宙中存活下來 , 我們將無法存活它們 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	僅僅是幾光年外的超新星爆炸 , 我們都將死 。
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁.瑞斯最近寫了一本關於我們對於各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗錯誤 , 最重要的是對於大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率能存活這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點會在研討會上討論這個主題 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的類別 , 來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他的看法 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們可以失敗的存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否能及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	這種危險完全不是前所未有的物種會絕種
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明就這樣結束了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有的文明都是現在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為例外的話 , 那麼邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望是利用區別我們族類和文明的這個特點 , 與其他所有其他的特徵--也就是 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	讓我把這套系統用在當前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提議任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是要說明我所要表達的 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議就是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是個對的物理學家 。 以全球暖化來說 , 我只是個地雷員 。 作為一個地雷員做的理性任務是認真看待普遍的科學理論 。 根據那個理論 , 避免災難已經太遲了 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果這是事實 , 我們目前最好的選擇就是防止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書、它對經濟活動的限制 , 以及它巨大的成本 , 不論是什麼 , 那都只是不合理的措施 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導這一點的行動根本不應該是為了解決問題 , 而僅僅只是延後一小部分而已 。 所以要避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 從來沒有人意識到它之前就已經無法避免它了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代早就已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放將促成一個數十億人會死亡的新冰河時代 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這件事對我來說是很顯而易見的 , 我不知道為什麼它不會告知大眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	這是我們永遠無法知道的 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何解決 , 遠低於災難本身的成本 , 那麼就沒有太多的爭議了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有任何預防措施 , 可以避免一些我們還沒有預測到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要停止治療 , 不僅僅是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防等於一盎司的治癒 , 但前提是我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你已經在鼻子上打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學並不是在教你如何避開拳頭 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學停止搜尋治癒 , 只專注於預防 , 那它也幾乎無法完成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界現在正忙著計畫不計代價將氣體排放的成本降低 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	可以大幅降低溫度 , 規劃可以大幅降低溫度 , 規劃可以降低溫度 , 不計成本 , 而是有效率又便宜 。 有些規劃的存在 , 像是大批的鏡子 , 可以偏轉陽光 , 並鼓勵水猿生物 , 多吃二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些都是邊緣的研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力解決這個問題的中心 , 也不是一般問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 能夠正確地做事的能力 , 不是無限期地避開好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 還包括生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿起兩塊石碑 , 刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 "
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它被困在不良規則的制度之下 , 一個掙扎的國家要如何瓦解 ? 經濟學家保羅羅默揭露一個大膽的概念: 「 特區城市 」 , 城市的行政區 , 由國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治 ,
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅羅•羅默極端的想法:特殊的都市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常迷人的益智遊戲 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在做功課在首都機場的路燈下進行作業因為他們家裡沒有電
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠襯衫的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以謎題來了 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以使用像手機這樣尖端的科技 ? 但在家中卻無法使用一百年的科技來製造電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡言之 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以阻止雙贏的解決方案在人們可以把新科技帶進像尼爾森這樣的人手上 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵循一套規則 , 說它必須以非常低、補貼的價格賣出電 , 事實上 , 它的價格非常低 , 賣出的每一單位都要價錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去幫許多其他用戶連結 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見識到 , 有可能有不同的規則、規則 , 讓企業獲利小 , 所以他們有動機去招募更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這是行動電話公司所遵守的原則 , nelson從下面操作他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則如何運作得很好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電價的規則 , 但卻碰到一連串的抗議活動 , 來自企業和消費者 , 他們想要維持現有的補助制度 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他卡在的規則中 , 阻止了他讓雙贏方案能協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在路燈下讀書 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	接下來真正的挑戰 , 是試著弄清楚如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則我們可以發展出改變制度的規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我認為有一種抽象的見解可以讓我們獲得實用 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人民更多選擇 , 對許多國家的領導者 , 更多的選擇也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但展示出這兩者對立場是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為那種選擇 , 你可能想要給領導人一種選擇 , 比如給總統提高電價的選擇 , 就能剝奪人民想要的經濟選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇可以繼續消耗政府補助的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只捐一邊或另一邊 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給予雙方更多的選擇 , 那就會給予我們一套規則 , 用來改變我們不再陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則破壞的影響 , 規則能讓人們保持在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署拍的照片 ,
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你拉近一點看這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 這裡跟它的鄰居比起來就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會驚訝地發現北韓的體制會讓那裡的人陷入黑暗 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但值得注意的是 , 北韓和南韓開始時有一套相同的規則 , 不論是法律或規範 , 更深層的意義 , 像是了解、規範、文化、價值觀 , 和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致了非常不同的路徑 , 形成他們制定的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變身為人類的我們 , 可以改變彼此互動的規則 , 改變彼此間的互動 , 變得更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地的畫面 , 在這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	這裡的海地也很暗 , 相對於它的鄰居多明尼加共和國數量也差不多
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家 , 相較於波多黎各 , 波多黎各有一半的居民是像海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是:規則可能不好 , 因為政府很軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不光是這些規則不好 , 因為政府的強勢和壓迫性 , 就像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造有良好規則的環境 , 我們就不能僅撕掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須想辦法建設
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	如今 , 中國戲劇性地展現出運用規則所帶來的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回溯到資料圖表的一開始 , 中國是世界上的高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人的科技像煉鋼、印刷、火藥等都是先驅
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則中 , 鼓勵那些想法散播出去的傳播 , 一個利潤動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播出去 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減慢了創新 , 把中國從世界其他地方砍下來 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 發展出新的科技 , 也發展了更新的規則 , 中國的進步已經被切斷了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入依然停滯不前 , 因為收入停滯在世界的另一端 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	顯示的是中國的平均所得佔美國平均所得的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代你可以看到它大約佔百分之三
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在七十年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的經濟開始起飛中國人開始迎頭趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到那個夜裡的地圖你就會發現這個過程會導致中國體制的巨大改變
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點也就是你們在輪廓邊上看到的這點是香港
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部份的時候 , 都採用非常不同的規則 , 相較於當時中國大陸原則 , 其規則在當時的勞動市場經濟中複製 , 並由英國政府施行 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在50年代 , 香港是一個讓數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 做一些工作 , 像是縫衣、玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了能增加收入 , 增加技能的過程會導致很快的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個例子 , 領導人如鄧小平可以複製 , 當他們決定將整個大陸推向市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個人立即轉換到市場模式 , 他們採取的做法是設立一些特殊區塊來做 , 某種程度上 , 英國所做的是:讓市場體制順利運作 , 讓那些想要選手的市政體制能夠順利運作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建立了四個經濟特區 , 讓中國人民可以來這裡工作 , 城市很快就在那裡成長 ; 外國企業也可以來這裡製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的其中一個城市叫做深圳 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那座城市中 , 有一間台灣企業 , 製造在座許多人都擁有的iphone , 他們是用從中國來勞動的 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	四個特別的區塊之後 , 有14個沿海城市 , 以相同的角度進行開放 , 最後在這些地方展示出成功的案例 , 人們可以選擇去的地方 , 他們因為提供的利益而聚集起來 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功促成了全體經濟向市場模式邁進的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了好幾個點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一 , 保存人民的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:操作的規模是對的 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村落的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但村落會太小 , 無法得到你所得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人都在做好的規則 , 你就會得到好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你想要改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給人們一個機會來支援 , 看看事情的結果 , 讓其他人放大一步 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市給你這個機會 , 來創造新地方 , 用新的規則 , 讓大家可以選擇去那裡 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	這些益處夠大 , 足以讓我們的所有利益在數百萬人一起合作的基礎規則下 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以提議我們構想一個所謂的特許城市 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	一開始 , 我們規劃了各項規則 , 來吸引我們建立城市所需要的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者來建設電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引企業他們才會先僱用移民者
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 來這裡的居民會永久地住在那裡 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著這一章節 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模式 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一次又一次的去做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它可行 , 我們需要良好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些是在憲章中被抓到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這個模式的確建立在無人居住地上 , 建立城市的可能性上 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的憲章底下生活 , 但沒有人會被迫在它底下生活 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們期望的領導者的樣子 , 我們需要擁有這種可能性 , 才能在國與國之間合作:事實上 , 在埃及和英國之間的合作 , 在中國和英國的合作 , 首先是市場模型的小奴隸 , 後來擴展到全中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國不經意地 , 透過香港的行動 , 來減少世界的貧窮 , 比上個世紀發生的所有援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們讓這樣的合作模式再度複製 , 我們就可以讓全世界都受惠 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會影響到負責任 , 將權力由一個國家授權給另一個國家 , 來接管某些特定的行政權 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始在想: 「 這是否能讓殖民主義恢復 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 , 但很重要的是要意識到 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的那種情緒 , 可能會阻礙我們回過頭去 , 可能會阻礙我們去移除我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這和殖民主義不同 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 仍然不好 , 那就是它牽涉到強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這種模式的重點在於選擇 , 對象 , 對住在新地方的領袖及人民而言都是如此 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而 「 選擇 」 是強迫和強迫的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談 , 要如何實現它 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	咱們來看看特定的領袖 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 她是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定也想過他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國所做的事情 , 但古巴並沒有像香港那樣的小島 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過他在南部有一點點光線 , 它的地位很特別 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣附近有一個區域 , 在那裡 , 一份條約為美國政府負責一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大的總理說: 「 看 , 南基斯有個嚴重的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要逃離 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼加拿大不接手呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特殊行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	在那裡建造一座新城市
allow many people to come in .	允許許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有一個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬到那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會退一步 , 但這將會是一座橋 , 將現代經濟與我國家的現代世界連結起來 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	這個模型還能在哪裡試用呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們大多完全了解特區的想法 , 讓大家可以選擇成一條規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是會改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新體制的方法 , 讓人民選擇沒有強制的力量 , 和強制的反對力量就能引起強制作用 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾 , 就像投資者會來蓋港口、在新城市建造道路 , 他們能做出更有保障的承諾 , 只要他們能和國家合作 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某些安排有點像信託管理帳戶 , 把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡 , 合作夥伴國也為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有很多的土地可以建造新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時照的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	這裡有像這樣的廣大土地 , 成千上萬的人能住的地方 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們簡化一下來想想 , 不只是一兩個特區公民 , 而是數十個城市 , 能為數億人創造空間 , 也許未來的數十億人會搬到城市去 , 有足夠的土地容納他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在全世界 , 如果我們看夜晚的燈光 , 其中一個誤導的就是 , 看來 , 大部分的世界是已經被建造出來的 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	用這塊土地來呈現所有的土地 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	而這些點代表的是有三十億人口居住在城市中的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到這個長方形的底部你會發現有30億人口的城市只佔了地球上可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要再為數十億人建造城市 , 就會變成像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	所佔的可耕地面積將從百分之三上升到百分之四
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大大減少了人類在地球上的足跡 , 藉由建造更多人們可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市遵守良好的規則 , 它們可以是城市的居民免受犯罪、疾病和衛生不良的威脅 , 人們就有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	像是電力這種基本公共事業 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一座特區城市 , 要如何擴大規模 , 才能建造出更多這樣的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	手冊就更好了 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的是撰寫一些關於這本手冊的細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理城市 , 走出去 , 設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會把學者趕出野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 比如 , 不只加拿大和卡斯楚的情況 。
