perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西也參加派對 , 而西班牙或許古巴想成為四邊合作的一員
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來做到這一點 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有前例可循 , 但那很容易就會被解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何去資助它 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	事實證明 , 新加坡和香港是二個城市在成立時獲得了巨大的收益 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的收益來支付像警察、法庭之類的費用 , 但學校體系和健康照護體系 , 這讓土地的居住環境更加吸引人 , 讓人們的收入更高 , 更加珍貴 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 對於協助建造這塊區域的人的鼓勵 , 建立它 , 並建立基礎規則 , 非常能走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	還有很多其它的細節
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓低成本且負擔得起的人在一開始工作 , 組裝成iphone , 讓建築更有效率 , 確保它們很安全 , 不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	很多技術上的細節尚待處理但我們這些已經開始追求這些事的人早已知道沒有路障了除了想像力失敗之外也無法阻礙我們提供真正的全球雙贏解決方案
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片作結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們會如此的幸福 , 即使地球上有很多人 , 都是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以跟別人分享想法當他們發現新點子 , 他們就跟我們分享
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 在那裡 , 分享意味著我們每個人都會變少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們這樣看待想法時 , 我們通常想到的是科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:主導我們如何互動的規則 ; 規則像是:我們有稅制系統 , 支持研究大學 , 免費提供某種知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓土地擁有一個系統 , 它能在政府機關上註冊 , 為人們發聲為 「 附屬 」 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷創新我們所在的規則 , 尤其是創新的概念 , 來制定改變的規則 , 所以我們不會卡在不良的規則中 , 那麼我們可以不斷進步 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不再需要在街燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	克萊格•凡特 , 先驅者從他的史詩般般的探險之旅中休息了一會兒 , 談到他的團隊目前為止發現的數百萬個基因 , 都在探索海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生態圈、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海洋上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	剛開始 , 有幾個人問我對於老化辯論的看法 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這是我唯一對此的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我知道樂觀者比悲觀者活得更久 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在18分鐘內要告訴你們的是我們如何從閱讀基因編碼轉換到開始自己編寫程式的第一階段
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅是10年前的一個月 , 我們發佈了第一組免費生存有機體的序列 , 即嗜血桿菌 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這項計畫花了13年才完成 , 才到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	現在我們可以執行同樣的基因組計劃 , 大約兩到八小時 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年 , 大量的基因組被加上:大部分的人類病原體 , 數種植物 , 數隻昆蟲和哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十年前 , 在這個階段的基因組學──到今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組的基因組定序 ; 數百個基因組的排序 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從grdon和bettymoore基金會的資助計畫得到今年的130組基因組定序 , 做為環境生物的附屬計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們觀察到 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓到這個星球上能找到的物體表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人不了解它 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔地球生物總量的一半 , 所有的動物只佔所有生物總量的一半左右 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	可能那是牛津人常常會做的事 , 但如果你曾經到海裡去 , 吞一口海水 , 別忘了每毫升的海水中都有大約一百萬隻細菌和大約一千萬隻病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	到兩年前 , 只有少於5000種微生物已經被定型 , 所以我們決定採取行動 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了蘇格拉二號探險 , 在那裡 , 我們進行大型的海洋探險 , 試圖每200英哩取樣海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始進行我們的測試計畫 , 接著移到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫跨太平洋 , 現在我們正在橫越印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常困難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上這麼做 , 有一部分原因是要讓年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是把海水和過濾器拿來取不同大小的微生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 我們可以每24小時完成一億個字母的基因編碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	通過這樣做 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 人們認為我們眼中的視覺色素環境中只有一兩種有機體擁有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界上上層海洋中的所有物種 , 都有相同的光感接受器 , 並將陽光當成它們的能量和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬種新基因 , 多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	目前我們已經從sloan基金會將這個計畫擴展到空氣中 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量我們每天所呼吸的病毒和細菌數量 , 尤其是在飛機上或密閉的觀眾席 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們從只有一天的時間點收集到的大約十億微生物 , 在紐約市的一棟大樓上過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於測序目前所有的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	在收集資料方面 , 我們穿過加拉巴哥群島的地方 , 我們發現幾乎每200英哩 , 我們在海裡看到巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	其中有些是合乎邏輯的 , 不同溫度的梯度 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這張是根據溫度的衛星照片--紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的--我們發現溫暖的水樣本和豐富的生物種類 , 兩者有極大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人驚訝的是這些色素細胞偵測不同波長的光線 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列預測出來 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些因素在不同地區都大大的變化 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在深海裡 , 大部分是藍色的光感接受器會看見藍色的光線 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化更大 , 可能更接近紅外線和紫外線 , 在極端 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因序列 , 我們把所有資料組合起來 , 包括我們目前在遠處的所有人 , 包括地球上一半以上的基因資料 , 總數約2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放到基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們僅僅是發現了已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但我們在環境中所採集的每一個新樣本 , 都是以線性的方式 , 為這些新家庭所提供的 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於發現基礎基因的最初階段 , 也是在這個星球上組成和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們在右上角 , 和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因只有兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物的基因組合起來 , 我們所共有的基因族群大約只有三萬不到一點 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	現在我認為這些基因不僅僅是進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們從基因中心來看 , 或許回到了理查•道金斯的想法 , 而不是基因組中心的觀點 , 這觀點不同於這些基因組成份的不同構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	製造dna的能力和dna定序速度差不多 , 和dna定序的速度差不多 , 過去十年或二十年間的速度差不多 , 而且變得非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們關於人工基因體的第一個想法是1995年我們對第二組基因組進行排序 , 而這是從真核桿菌生殖器中得到的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面說: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們會問的問題是 , 如果一個物種需要800個 , 另一個500種 , 有沒有一組比較小的基因組 , 會是由最小的運作系統所組成 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨機插入基因密碼的一小段dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果插入基因的正中間 , 會阻斷其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張所有可以轉位子插入的基因地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明環境是至關重要的而且只能依據環境的特性來定義一個必要或非必要的基因
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們還嘗試了更直接的方法來研究13種相似有機體的基因組 , 我們試著比較這些基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這個重疊的圓圈 。 我們找到的只有173個基因 , 佔據了13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果不算其中一種細胞寄生蟲的話 , 這個池子會稍微擴大一點 , 當我們研究核心基因組時 , 大約310組左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以根據你們的觀點 , 擴展或收縮基因組 , 到大約300到400個基因 , 從最小的500個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是用這些基因建造一個人造染色體 , 我們必須依照一種基礎的方法來做 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 合成精確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison在我的同事們研發出令人振奮的新方法可以讓我們在兩週內製造5000個鹼基對的病毒而它的序列和生物學上的精確度是100%
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這實驗非常令人振奮 , 當我們採用人造的dna , 注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始製造病毒粒子轉動 , 殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這還不是人造病毒的初期 , 小兒麻痺病毒在一年前被製造出來 , 但它只有原始成本的千分之一 , 花了三年才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	軟體現在打造它自己的硬體 , 這就是我們生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上開始關心生物戰爭 , 最近我在參議院委員會前發表了證詞 , 還有一個美國政府設立的特殊委員會來檢視這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 把現實留在心中 , 對比人們的想像會是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今任何已經被定序過的病毒 , 其基因組可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會對於伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐 , 但這個生物的dna不是有效的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使製造出天花的基因體 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓人擔憂的是安全部門的設計病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	僅有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 極大努力想要創造生物武器元件 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那些研究真的被終止了 , 將來在製造設計病毒上 , 應該不會再有甚麼進展了 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞生物是可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而很有可能的真核細胞在十年內就有可能實現 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以現在我們正在做數十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以改變這些放入人造染色體的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 如何盡其所能 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 然後有一個整體重組系統 , 將這些片段重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這源自一種生物 , 也就是耐輻射奇異球菌 , 它能承受三百萬雷得的輻射 , 不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發過後 , 它會在12至24小時內重新組合它的基因組 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上普遍存在 , 或許是因為我們旅行的所有過程而存在於外太空 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是經過50萬拉德輻射照射過後的一個玻璃杯
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始碎裂 , 玻璃底部的微生物變得越來越快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際狀況的圖片上面的圖片顯示的是經過一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被爆炸了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	的確令人吃驚的是 , 這些生物能夠做到這一點 , 我們可能有成千上萬 , 甚至上萬種不同的生物 , 能夠做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被製造之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 也希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們測序的第三個生物上 , 詹納西里發現了生命的沸騰的水溫 ; 其能量來源是氫 , 其碳是從環境中獲取的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 成千上萬種不同的生物 , 以二氧化碳為生 , 並能將其捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 我們不採用石油來進行合成處理 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 將它從大氣層中捕捉回來 , 轉化成生物高分子或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物 , 存在於一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來當作降低能分解水來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多種途徑 , 可以改造成甲烷的代謝 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	dupont在挪威使用石油來捕捉和轉換這些來自天然氣場的甲烷成為有用的產品
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我想會有一個新的領域叫做 「 組合基因體 」 , 因為這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因排列和同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可以製造上百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 正如所有生物學一樣 , 你可以通過篩選來得到選擇 , 不論是對氫氣產生或化學生產 , 或只是生存 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的作用 , 將是非常容易的 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用從陽光直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程的氧氣 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也將纖維素和分解複合的酵素分解成單糖、發酵在同一個細胞中 , 來產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	用微生物進行製藥生產的實驗室已經在各大實驗室中進行 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	來自環境中的化合物的化合物排序比我們所生產的最好的化學家排序還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 也許取代了石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策來作結 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審核是否應該嘗試製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這真的是一項非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都用他們的教義作為法律 , 他們無法在書中找到任何能禁止生命的條款 , 所以這也沒關係 。 最終的卻是生物戰的方面的擔憂 , 只能給我們預先進行這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	如今sloan基金會已經資助了一個多機構的研究 , 用來找出對社會有何風險和利益 , 以及一些科學團隊所做的規則 , 例如我自己的團隊應該在這個領域使用 , 我們正在嘗試建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們是否能設計產品來產生乾淨能源 , 或許改革開發中國家能夠做些什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說幸福和成功是根植於我們大多數人不認同的特徵:我們朝向過去、現在和未來邁進的方式 。 他建議我們把自己的觀點當成改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心、心理、心理、科學 ,
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo處方一個健康的時代 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量 , 很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始計時 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間快到了 。 再來一次 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 8 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:讓我們調整一下這段對話的主題 , 來談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 不要那麼希望 , 吃一口 。 」 「 我有 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口 。 搞什麼鬼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑的 。 重點是要產生 , 抵抗 , 是的 , 現在 , 以後 , 衝動 , 關注現在 , 和未來 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	保證美德會勝過當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	一些青少女 , 曾宣誓要在婚前要感謝布什 , 絕大多數 , 約有60% , 會在一年內帶著性別的誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	而他們大多數都沒有採取避孕措施 。
so much for promises .	太多的承諾了 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在來試試四歲的小孩 , 給他們吃得好了 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到試驗員回來 , 就會有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 那就得等下 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的狀況是三分之二的孩童對誘惑感到誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 , 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 延遲了當下的行為 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	我在史丹佛大學的同事沃爾特•米歇爾14年後 , 試圖找出這些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	那些抗拒的孩子和那些用各種方式來產生巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抗拒在sat考試成績250分的孩子 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很了不起 。 這就像一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有太多麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	她們是自信且有堅定的 。 而對我來說 , 關鍵是 , 她們是以 " 未來為主 " 為主而非 " 立即 " 為主 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時間觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	看待時間角度是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你人生經歷的流向切分為時區或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動且無意識地進行 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水準之間有不同的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會產生偏見 , 因為你會學會過度使用 , 忽略其他的部分 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在當下情況 , 別人做的事和你的感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們做出那樣的決定 , 我們就要稱他們為 「 現實導向 」 , 因為他們關注的是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是無關緊要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	重要的是: 「 我過去的經歷是什麼樣子的 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 " 懷舊主義 " , 因為他們關注的是過去 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對於另一些人 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 而是未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們專注於所期待的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們關注的是未來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是時間觀點的悖論是會影響你做出的每一個決定 , 而你完全沒意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有這種偏頗的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	實際上 , 總共有六種解釋方式 。 有兩種解釋方式可以用在當下 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種神秘主義的方式 , 兩種變成未來的方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以注重 " 正面懷舊 " 或 " 負面懷舊 "
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	也可以是 " 享受主義者 " , 也就是專注於生活的喜悅 , 或是不重要的是懷舊主義者 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 " 理想主義 " , 設定目標
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者你也可以是超然的未來即 , 生命從死後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 來改變時間觀點 , 根據情境的需求而定 , 這就是你要學的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " 、 " 適度 " 的未來 " 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是把負面和現代主義降低 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳時光的混合是你從過去積極的事物中得來的 。 將你的家庭、身份 , 和你的自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來得到的是發翅目 , 飛向新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的能量就是探索你自己、地方、人、感性
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度的時間觀點都有負面而非積極 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來要犧牲什麼才能成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友時光 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂時光 ; 犧牲個人的贖罪 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲業餘愛好 ; 犧牲睡眠 。 所以會影響到他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為工作、成就和控制而生 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 那會和一些ted成員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我產生共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯貧民窟長大 , 西西里島家庭 , 過去和現在都是 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我是以未來的身份來到頂端的人 , 做出這些犧牲 , 只因為老師介入 , 讓我有朝一日的未來 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你在等待你就會得到其中二顆 , 直到我學會去平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我把焦點放在正面 , 所以 , 七十六歲時 , 我比以往更有活力、更有生產力 , 而我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們正在把這個應用在許多世界的問題上:改變輟學率 , 對抗毒品 , 增加青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療退伍軍人 , 用奇蹟來治療永續和保育 , 減少身體康復率 , 上升的比率是50% , 改變自殺式恐怖份子的死亡率 , 以及修正家庭關係 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想說 , 人生的謎題可以解決 , 只要了解你的時間觀和其他人的觀點 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	很簡單 , 很顯而易見 , 但我認為結果非常深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	今天的頭條有多少在一百年內很重要 ? 一千年後呢 ? 克雷克-頓的 「 長新聞 」 計畫收集到現今不只如此 , 也會引起數十年前的回應 。 在ted2010年 , 他提到近期的頭條標題有可能會影響我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學 ,
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 還有真實的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社一年就發佈三百五十萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	這只是其中一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事當中有多少個在長期來說是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	那就是 「 長遠新聞 」 的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個由長遠現在基金會發起的專案 , 由tedsters包括kevinkelly和stewartbrand 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們期待的新聞報導可能在50或100或10 , 000年之後仍然很重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	而當你透過篩選器來檢視新聞時 , 許多東西都落在了兩邊 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	拿去年美聯社的頭條新聞來說 , 十年後這還會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那還滿酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年的頭條是經濟 , 我敢說 , 遲早 , 這波經濟衰退將會是老式的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 就以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 微型機器人會穿過我們的血液管道來補救東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是一隻老鼠 , 就已經有一天了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近的故事是:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液將基因送入大腦 ; 他們製造的機器人可以在人體上爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何養活90億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今餵飽了60億人的麻煩 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億的人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國在沒有基改作物的情況下挨餓 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	還好比爾蓋茲投資了10億美元在農業研究上
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會變得非常不一樣 , 如果中國設立了議程 , 且可能會發生 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們已經開始對孩子們進行dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在尋找各種方法來把我們所知道的限制推回 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近有些發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群現在散播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 自導導的機器人科學家很快就有了發現 , 科學可能就不再需要我們了 , 生活可能也不再需要我們了 ; 十二萬年後 , 出現了微生物 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎沒有人類 , 生命就會延續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但去年 , 我挑選了 「 長遠新聞 」 的頭條是:在月球上有水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	要把一個蟻群放到上面來 , 就容易多了 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果太空總署不做 , 中國可能會做 , 或這間房間的人可能會做檢查 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:從長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家carolynporco顯示卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 聚焦在它最大的衛星泰坦大衛 , 及結凍土衛二 , 它似乎拍攝冰噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化圖像 ,
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡洛琳.波洛科請我們飛往土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我將帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	你和我已經進行了許多年的旅程 , 50年前 , 人類第一次踏出地球時 , 這旅程就開始了 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅成功地登上了月球 , 我們還將太空船和8個行星分離 , 降落在小行星上 , 我們與彗星相遇 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船正向冥王星邁進 , 之前稱之為行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類更大的旅程之一 。 我們航行的目的是理解事物 , 理解宇宙 , 理解我們的起源 , 了解我們的地球 , 和我們賴以維生的地球 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	太陽系中所有我們想去的地方 , 找尋類似問題的答案 , 例如土星 。 我們曾到過土星 。 1980年代初期我們拜訪過土星 , 但我們對土星的研究已經變得更加深入細節 。 卡西尼號太空船穿梭於行星之間長達七年之久 , 在2004年的夏天中 , 駕駛於軌道上 , 成為人類曾經建造過的最遠離地球機器人 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個很豐富的地球系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞察 , 並且顯然超出對比 , 而這個系統的調查 , 有很大的宇宙範圍 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是去研究光環 , 我們就能夠學到很多關於星星和氣體圓盤的知識 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的照片是仙女座星系 , 這是我們最接近的 , 也是銀河系裡最大型的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這裡有一幅漂亮的旋風星系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以回到土星的這段旅程 , 也是一個比喻 , 比喻了人類更大的旅程 , 目的是要了解我們身邊所有事物的相互連結 , 以及人類是如何融合這張圖片的 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們用卡西尼學過的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半所拍攝的所有美麗照片 , 因為我根本沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	我會專注於這次大型探索之旅當中出現的兩件最令人振奮的故事 , 是我們繞著土星進行的 , 長達兩年半之久 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著非常大多樣的衛星組合 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里到大不等於美國 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝土星的美麗照片事實上 , 土星和它的衛星 。 這是土星和土星和土衛二 。 這是土星和土衛二的光環 , 這裡是土衛二的直線 , 告訴你它們有多薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	如今 , 土星47顆衛星有兩顆發光裝置 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六泰坦和土衛二 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 它是我們在太陽系中最大的未被探勘過的單獨地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是長期以來觀看這些行星的人們著迷的身體 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像我們地球上的環境 , 至少在過去 , 比其它太陽系中的天體更接近 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣中含有大量氮分子 , 如同你在這裡所呼吸的氮氣 , 只不過它的大氣中有許多簡單的有機物質如甲烷、丙烷、丙烷和乙烷等 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在泰坦的大氣層中會被分解 , 它們的產物結合在一起 , 製造出迷霧的粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這混亂無所不在 , 完全是全球且包圍的霸主 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能用肉眼看到的光譜區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀的粒子在卡西尼號到達之前 , 是被推測出來的 , 在我們和卡西尼在那裡之前 , 已經經過數十億年 , 溫和地漂浮到地表上 , 覆蓋在厚實的有機物當中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像泰坦的焦油、油 , 或是我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們所猜測的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六表面的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是 「 土衛六 」 的標準 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可以冷凝的 , 所以 , 認識到這種情形之後 , 帶來了非常多奇怪的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲之上 , 幾百公里高的霧氣 , 可以阻止陽光進入表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管很冷 , 土衛六上還是會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在地球上 , 降雨的原因是:它會切開水溝 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能形成峽谷 ; 大型盆地 , 大型盆地 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它能把泥土從高山的山峰上沖到低地帶 。 所以停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子的 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	那裡一片漆黑 , 土衛六上的正中午也和地球上的黑暗一樣 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 陰陽、陰森 , 陰陽可能正在下雨 , 而你可能正站在密西根湖邊 , 旁邊有油漆稀疏的密西根湖邊 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們和卡西尼一起到達土衛六之前的樣子 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現的 , 儘管它的細節和故事的內容不一樣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼人──那就像是青少年凡爾納的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是土衛六的背 , 背在太陽的背景下 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個衛星我甚至不知道是哪一個 。 它是非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器能看到表面 , 穿過大氣層 , 我的攝影機就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 且那差不多對我們而言是如此 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這真是太迷人了:我們無法找出我們看到的鐵達尼號 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近一點看這塊區域 , 你會看到一些東西 , 像是無人的管道 。 我們並不知道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 這原來是一個坑洞 , 但土衛六表面積很少有隕石坑 , 意即 , 土衛六的表面很年輕 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有看起來像是地殼的特徵 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來像是被拆解了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	不論你在地球上看到什麼線性的東西 , 這就表示有個骨折 , 例如一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經被地質性地改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的圖像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一件事件發生了 , 許多人都認為它是卡西尼研究土衛六的亮光 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是惠更斯探測器的發射 , 歐洲自造的惠更斯探測器橫跨了太陽系七年 。 我們把它發射到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時才降落 , 結果到地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想要強調這件事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類史上第一次有人造的裝置降落在外太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我心中 , 這實在是太重要了 , 我本來應當舉辦一場活動 , 為美國和歐洲各城市的滴答遊行舉辦 。 真是令人難過 , 但事實並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很重要 , 基於另一個原因 。 這是個國際使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國被讚頌 , 慶祝用英語發表的簡報 , 和美國口音、德國口音、法語、義大利和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是一個關於 " 聯合國 " 應該要有的字眼展示:一個國家的真實結合 , 以大眾利益為出發 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探索一個星球是一項龐大任務 , 為了了解一個星球系統 , 對於人類歷史來說 , 這個星球是不可修補的 , 而現在 , 人類已經觸動了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我會起雞皮疙瘩就談這件事 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	這是非常劇烈的情緒事件 , 而這是我永遠不會忘記的 , 你們也不該如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	探測器在降落過程中對大氣進行了測量 , 並且拍攝了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看見第一張土衛六地表的照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這很令人震驚 , 因為這已經是我們所期待的 , 從軌道上拍攝的所有照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是個明確的模式 , 地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這種樹枝狀的排水模式只能透過液體的流動來形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些管道看看它們如何匯合 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們匯合到這裡的水道中 , 滲透到這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍攝的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里的高度拍攝的 , 看 , 還是一樣 , 是海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--大概是一架航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫跨美國 , 你可能會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	所以 , 這就是你在鐵達尼亞航空公司的窗戶上所能看到的景象 , 就在飛越土衛六的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器終於停在表面了 , 我會給你們看 , 女士們先生們 , 這張照片是從外太陽系衛星表面拍下來的第一張衛星照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	顯然 , 降落在一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 卻沒有降落到我們目的地 。 所以液體不是我們著陸的 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上下降的探測器就像是泥土的巨型平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這塊地充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能這種材料已經從土衛六的高地沖刷過 , 經過我們看到的這些通道 , 且排乾了數十億年 , 才能填滿低窪地帶 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 仍然沒有在我們的影像中看到 , 甚至在惠更斯的影像中也沒有任何大型開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	牠們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人費解 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	這是我們電影中的赤道地區的地形 , 這些沙丘的高度100公尺 , 由幾公里高的沙丘分離出來 , 它們跑上幾英里 , 長達數英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	幾百英里高達一千到一千兩百英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然它是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者是你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 這讓人感到困惑 , 沒有液體 , 直到我們終於看到北極地區的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	這是土衛六南極的一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	它和安大略湖差不多大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 就在一週半前 , 我們飛越北極 , 發現了相當於加勒比海的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	看來這些液體 , 是因為我們不明白的原因 , 或者至少這個季節 , 在泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現泰坦是個不可思議、神秘的地方 。 它很奇怪 , 它很奇怪 , 但又和地球很相似 , 有類似地球的地形和極大的地理多樣性 , 且這個神奇的世界是太陽系中太陽系中唯一相對的和豐富性才是地球 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們到土衛二上 。 土衛二是個小衛星 , 大小約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它在英國旁邊 , 只是讓你們看看它的大小 。 這不應該是個威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二很白很亮 , 它的表面有很明顯的裂痕 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質上非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多集中在南極 , 而我們現在看到的是南極 , 我們發現了這個系統地裂 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們的成分不同 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被塗層 , 這些骨折被有機材料塗層 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極地帶的溫度上升了 , 溫度在地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這有點奇怪 , 因為我們發現地球上的南極是比熱帶地區還熱的 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 我們拍攝了更多照片 , 我們發現從這些地裂中 , 有細小的冰粒噴射出來 , 噴射到太空中數百英里 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們為這張圖做顏色編碼時 , 要拿出微弱的光線 , 我們會看到這些噴射流在土衛二上方數千英里的空間中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊檢視了像這樣的圖片 , 和這張圖片 , 還想過了卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是 , 這些風暴可能是從土衛二地表下的液態水坑噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們可能有液態水、有機物質和過剩的熱量 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們有可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 也就是說 , 一個可能適合生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中其它地方 , 不論是土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有很大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 " 創世紀 " 已經發生了不止一次 , 而是兩次獨立在我們的太陽系裡 , 那麼假設在整個宇宙中 , 它已經發生了相當驚人的數量 , 而它137億年來的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍是唯一一顆充滿生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴、獨一無二 , 它至今仍然是我們唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們中有人在60年代時警覺且一致 , 我們原諒你們 , 如果沒有的話 , 你們會記得1968年阿波羅八號太空人拍下的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空中拍攝地球 , 並對我們在宇宙中的位置有極大的衝擊 , 我們對於保護地球的責任感是有極大的衝擊 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們的卡西尼號同樣拍下了一張前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是日全蝕從土星的另一側拍攝的
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可思議的美麗照片中 , 你看到背後的主光 , 看到太陽的折射影像 , 還可以看到由土衛二的揭露出來的光環 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 就好像這還不夠聰明 , 我們還能在這美麗的圖像中看到我們自己的星球 , 時而動搖在土星光環的臂彎中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	對於從遠處看我們自己有某種深刻的感動並捕捉到我們在其他星球的視覺影像 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而這個 , 我們對自己的看法 , 可能是從這次旅程得到的最好的獎賞 , 是我們從這次旅程開始的半個世紀 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被繪製圖 。 這很緩慢的援助 , 還隱藏未被使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在這簡短的演講中 , 谷歌的拉特加達demosss-全球各地的團體工具被用來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的卡特加達:對抗災難的地圖 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 颶風納格破壞了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人極度需要協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人民和物資趕到那個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖、沒有道路地圖、沒有地圖顯示醫院、沒有地圖協助受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 全世界只有15%的人被配對到可數位的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國也解決了一個世界大部分的人口問題:沒有詳盡的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 救兵來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 有40個自願者使用了一套軟體標註了12萬公里的道路3000間醫院 , 物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的軟體呢 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一種能賦予我們每個人在當地所知的科技 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體標註了道路 , 河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 到視頻到轉角的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎被提名人hernandodesoto認爲開發中國家的經濟利益是去掌握大量未清潔的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度就有價值一兆美元的房地產不屬於資產 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	單單在去年170個國家數千個使用者就標註了數百萬個訊息並創造了前所未見的細節地圖
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這一切都是因為充滿熱情的使用者無所不在的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	咱們現在就來看看使用者的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	在這170個國家中 , 人們畫出世界地圖
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑剛剛為塞內加爾標註了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家近一點的地方 , chalua是bangalore的一個國家公路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何、手勢辨識 , 以及機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數千名使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是個邀請 , 邀請我們有70%未開發的星球 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新的世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落於巴勒斯坦一個月長達十個月的非暴力抗爭中 , 阻止了他的和平 。 你聽到了嗎 ? 沒有想到這點嗎 ? 巴西的電影製作人朱利亞•巴夏查問為什麼我們只注意到以色列抗爭的暴力 , 而不是等同一天會帶來和平的非暴力領袖 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞•巴夏:專注在非暴力的議題上 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦試圖用和平的方式來結束衝突的人們 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國各地旅行時 , 總是會有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	我聽到這個問題時 , 遇到的挑戰是我剛從中東回來 , 拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和居民 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正試著擺脫一個大規模的國家非暴力運動 , 來終止這個地區的佔領 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 你們多數人可能沒聽說過這些事 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	實情和國外正在發生的事情之間的分歧 , 正是造成我們還沒有一場巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動成功的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天要來談關注的力量你的關注的力量和非暴力運動在約旦河西岸加薩和其它地方的出現與發展而今日我所做的個案將是巴勒斯坦
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 要促進非暴力運動 , 最少的不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經是非暴力手段的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我帶你到這個名為布德魯斯的村落來說明這一點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈要築起一道隔離屏障 , 部分在這個村子的上面 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並被包圍 , 如此一來 , 他們就能自由地失去剩下的約旦河西岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過受啟發的當地領導人他們發動了和平抗爭活動來阻止這事發生
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 你們可以了解在地面上到底是什麼樣子的 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們聽說 , 牆將分隔巴勒斯坦和以色列 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村 , 我們了解到這堵牆將竊取我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:柵欄其實是解決恐懼的一個方法 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	第一個人:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你加入了數十位你的以色列兄弟姐妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:軍隊害怕的就是非暴力抗爭 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試著推開那些士兵 , 但是他們都無法做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女生們能做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空思考的心智 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們很和諧 , 我們想把這些都散播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號聲:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和受歡迎的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:圍牆上的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們可以使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是即時子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是費洛蒙 。 到處都射擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列抗議人士:我確定我們都要死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但有些身邊的人甚至一點都不害怕 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭無法阻止這【不清楚】
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們做得到 ! 我們做得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴夏:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很意外 , 國際媒體報導的一系列事件在七年前 , 2003年發生了一系列事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民抗爭十個月後說服了以色列政府將這道牆從他們的土地移開到綠線上也就是國際公認的以色列和巴勒斯坦領土間的界線
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此散播到整個西岸的村落 , 以及耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦人鄰居 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然對這些故事一無所知 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默帶來了很大的結果 , 影響非暴力可能會成長、甚至在巴勒斯坦生存的可能性 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點 , 它們都是劇院目的在觀眾的原因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果只有在頭版新聞 , 才能吸引國際媒體對巴勒斯坦的關注 , 對非暴力領袖會變得很難向他們的社區實現主張公民抗命是個可行的選項 , 要處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能不會讓房間裡的父母感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要確保你的孩子會吵得更大聲一點 , 一定要先給他注意力 , 那是他第一次拋出適當的心理 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	這種拉丁語會變成童年心理學家所說的功能性行為 , 因為孩子知道他能藉此得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能透過提供注意力或吸引孩童注意力來鼓勵或抑制行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇聚焦在關注的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 結束中東的衝突並帶來和平的核心 , 就是要把非暴力行動轉化為有用的行為 , 做法是要讓非暴力的領袖更重視當代的領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	當我拍攝約旦河西岸的村子、加薩及東耶路撒冷的村子時 , 我就看見了即使是一部紀錄片也能影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在瓦拉杰村 , 座落在非常接近耶路撒冷的村落 , 這個社區面對的是和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 沒有自由可用 , 可能是向西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用了兩年的非暴力手段 , 但已經被放棄了 , 因為沒有人注意到 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一份螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後他們舉辦了目前為止最有權力和紀律的示威
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	舉辦人說村民見到布德鲁斯村的故事記錄了一部影片 , 覺得確實有人在跟隨他們的腳步 , 有人在乎的 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這邊有一個新的和平運動叫做sorlidariot , 意即在希伯來語中 , 保持團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直在使用布德鲁斯村是他們主要的工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導過去從未參與過的以色列人看過電影時了解到非暴力的力量並加入他們的活動
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索里德拉爾特的獨立製片的例子顯示即使只是小小的預算 , 也可以讓非暴力行為轉變成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 如果他們開始報導這些每週都在村子裡進行的非暴力遊行 , 像是比爾本、尼林、瓦拉耶 , 在耶路撒冷的耶路撒冷地區 , 像謝赫克拉和西華這些非暴力領導人 , 在他們的工作中 , 會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我已經首先看到 , 如果我們能做到 , 它們會繁殖 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果它們繁殖 , 它們的影響會在以色列和巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力就是那種能夠釋放情況的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力是可行的 , 如布德鲁斯村 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	咱們來關注他們 , 讓他們能在任何地方證明它是可行的 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙奈克有個簡單而強大的模式 , 能鼓舞人心的領導 , 始於黃金圈和 「 為什麼 」 , 他的例子包括蘋果 , 馬丁路德金 , 和萊特兄弟 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	公事、商業、企業家、領導力、銷售、銷售、成功、
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	simonsinek:偉大的領導者如何啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	如果事情不如我們所想的那樣 , 你要如何解釋 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠完成似乎違反所有假設的情況 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	舉例來說:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比其他競爭對手都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	但 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	它們就跟大家一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們對有同樣才華的人有相同的管道 , 同樣的機構 , 同樣的顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼為什麼他們似乎有什麼不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到平等待遇的人而且他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼是萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權 , 操控飛機當飛機上有其他團隊更有資格 , 更有資金
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現人類飛行的成就 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法而它甚至深深改變了我在其中的運作方式
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	事實證明 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果是 , 世界上所有偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁•路德•金恩或萊特兄弟 , 他們都用同樣的方式來思考、行動和溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全和所有其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是把它編碼 , 很可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠激勵其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這些詞彙 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織 , 都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道如何做 , 不論你稱它為你不同的價值主張、屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或機構知道他們為什麼要做他們所做的 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 並不是 「 為了賺錢 。 」
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 它永遠是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的起因是什麼 ? 你的信仰是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	因此 , 我們思考的方式、行為的方式、我們溝通的方式都是由外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚到最模糊不明 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但受啟發的領導者和受到啟發的組織 , 不論它們的規模 , 不論它們的產業都認為 , 行動和溝通從內而外來 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果是因為它很容易懂 , 而每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦就像其他人一樣 , 來自它們的行銷訊息聽起來就像這樣: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們有著完美的設計 , 簡單的使用 , 和使用者友善的使用 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 「 梅 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷手段的做法多數銷售手段也就是多數人際溝通的方式
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說 , 我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買行為、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的法律事務所:我們有最好的律師 , 裡面有最大客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶做表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很好的氣體里程數 , 有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這裡是蘋果實際溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品有美好的設計 , 簡單的使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣嗎 ? 你準備從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	這證明了人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在場的每個人都對買蘋果電腦感到很自在 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒服地買蘋果的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果公司的手機或蘋果公司的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	正如我之前所說 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區別它們在任何競爭者身上的結構性 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出了平面電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	它們很明顯有資格製造平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經做平面螢幕好幾年了 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾電腦是由mp3播放器和pda所組成的 , 他們生產的品質很棒 , 他們能做出完美設計好的產品 , 但沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼要買一家電腦公司的mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是與每個需要你的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是與相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	以下是最好的部分:我告訴你們的都不是我的想法 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這都是從生物學上來的 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的橫斷面 , 從上往下看 , 看到的是人腦 , 事實上是分裂成三個主要元素 , 完美地與黃金圈對立 。
