our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們的最新大腦、我們人類的大腦、我們的大腦、皮層 , 都對應到 「 什麼 」 層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦皮層負責我們所有理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成我們邊緣的腦 , 而我們邊緣的腦 , 負責所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為、所有決策 , 且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特色、好處、事實、數字等 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它就是無法驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通時 , 我們直接與大腦對話 , 來控制行為 , 然後我們允許人們合理化它 , 用我們所說和所做的有形事物 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	決策就是這樣來的 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會給別人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有的事實和細節 , 但那感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用這個動詞 , 不會覺得 「 感覺對 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦並不控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最多能整理出的是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你會說你在帶著你的心 , 或者你在帶著你的靈魂領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想跟你們說 , 那些不是身體的其他部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你邊緣的腦裡 , 控制決策的腦 , 而不是語言的控制 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你做你所做的事 , 人們會回應為什麼你做你所做的事 , 那麼你要如何才能讓人們為你投票 , 或是向你買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 要忠誠 , 且想要成為你所做的事情的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你所擁有的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不是只在雇用需要工作的人而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 你知道的 , 如果你雇用員工 , 因為他們可以做事 , 他們會為了你的錢而做事 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們就會用血汗和眼淚來替你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有比萊特兄弟更好的例子了 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpierpontlangley的故事
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在20世紀初 , 人類飛行的追求就像當時的網路公司一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有 , 我們假設的成功的關鍵
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你也會問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你同樣的三件事:不資本化、不合適的人、不良的市場環境 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	這三件事都是一樣的 , 所以讓我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley從國防部得到5萬美金 , 想出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	資金根本沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他擔任哈佛大學的席位 , 並且在史密森工作 , 並且有很好的連結 ; 他認識當時所有的大人 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的人才資金 , 而市場狀況非常好 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑而且每個人都為langley加油
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠在俄亥俄州的華盛頓萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功關鍵 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用自行車店裡的收入來支付他們的夢想 ; 萊特兄弟的一個人沒有大學教育 , 甚至沒有大學維爾或威爾伯 ; 而紐約時報的追蹤則完全沒有 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 歐維爾和威爾伯是有目的、由信念所驅動的 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能想出這架飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同了 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人用血汗和淚水和他們一同努力 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了賺錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是 , 每次萊特兄弟出門 , 他們就得拿出五套零件 , 因為這是他們在出門前會墜機的次數 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛 , 甚至沒有人在那兒體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明langley的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟在飛行那天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 這真是很了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他辭職 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談論你所相信的事物 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人是很重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂創意的散播法則 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你絕對知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	首先我們人口中有2.5%的人口是發明家 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是早期使用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的多數 , 是晚期的多數 , 或晚期的落後者 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	人們買觸控電話的唯一理由是你再也買不了輪迴電話 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們在不同地方的規模上都坐在不同的地方 , 但創新的擴散法卻告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你不能擁有它 , 直到你達到了在15%到18%之間的市場侵入點 , 然後系統就會一躍而下 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是多少 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很樂意對你說: 「 喔 , 大致上是10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以旅行超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有百分之十的 「 了解 」
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣來描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就好像那種直覺的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們只是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到那些在做生意之前就先拿到的人 ? 問題是那些沒有拿到的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	就是這裡 , 一個小小的差距 , 如同傑佛瑞•摩爾所說的 , 「 跨越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期的多數人都不會嘗試直到其他人先嘗試 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人、發明家、早期採用者 , 他們很自在地做這些決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們對做這些直覺的決定感到更自在 , 驅動著他們對世界的信念 , 而不只是產品的現況 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排了六個小時 , 才剛上市的時候買了一支iphone , 下星期你還可以走進商店 , 還從架上買一台 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人剛上市時花了四萬美金在平面電視上即使科技還不夠實用
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們不這麼做是因為這項科技很棒 , 他們自己這麼做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要當第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼做 , 和你做什麼就證明了你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買iphone在最初的六個小時排隊排六個小時是因為他們所相信的這個世界以及他們希望每個人怎樣看他們:他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個有名的例子一個有名的失敗以及有名的成功關於創意的散播法則
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業化的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們前面所說的 , 成功的關鍵就是金錢、對的人、對的市場環境 , 對嗎 ? 你當時應該要有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	大約八、九年前 , tivo上市至今 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手放手 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	資金非常充足 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場環境好得不得了 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是tivo東西在我時代華納的垃圾上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo卻失敗了 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	他們上了ipo , 股價約是30到40美元 , 然後壓縮 , 從未在10美元以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為在六個以上交易 , 除了幾個小突點 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們的產品可以暫停現場電視 , 跳過商業廣告 , 轉播電視 , 記住你的收視習慣 , 連問都沒有 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你生活各個層面的人 , 我們有一項產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它可以暫停現場電視、跳過商業廣告、記住你的收視習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅是你相信什麼的證明 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你一個成功的例子關於創意的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年的夏天 , 25 , 000人在華盛頓的購物中心會聽到金恩博士的演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何一張邀請函 , 卻沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是在美國唯一一個偉大的演說家
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受到公民權利影響的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的想法有一些很糟的 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	那些相信他所相信的人們接受了他的觀點 , 使它成為他們自己的目標 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了一些結構 , 讓更多人知道 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25 , 000人在正確的日子裡 , 能聽到他說話的聲音 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人會為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了他們自己出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們認為的美國 , 讓他們搭公車旅行了八個小時 , 在八月中時站在華盛頓的陽光下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人25%的觀眾是白人
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種不同的法律:那些由較高權威制定的法律 , 那些由人所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有人類所制定的法律與更高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們將生活在一個公平的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正巧公民權運動是幫助他賦予他生命的最佳因素 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治家用完整的12點計畫
they're not inspiring anybody .	它們不會啟發任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導者啟發我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織我們跟隨那些領導的人不是因為我們必須而是因為我們想要
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	是那些以 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能啟發他們身邊的人 , 或找到鼓舞他們的人的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要怎麼記住車子停在哪裡 ? 你要怎麼知道你正朝著正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家尼爾•伯格爾在研究我們周圍的神經機制 , 以及他們如何與記憶和想像有關聯 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•伯格斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在大型停車場停車場停車時 , 我們要如何記住我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬現在有問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們將會試著去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 在黃色標記的黃色部分 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你的損害像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你記不得包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是以拉丁文 " 海馬 " 命名的 , 相似之處 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	如同其餘的腦 , 它是由神經元所構成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人腦內有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元藉由脈衝或電脈衝互相傳遞訊息彼此
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞間非常緊密的連結組成 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家也開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的藉由記錄老鼠在環境中覓食或探索找尋食物時的個別神經元的記錄
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像我們紀錄單一個神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體中
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一小塊電點 , 就會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到這個神經元知道當老鼠進入某個特定的環境時 , 老鼠就會知道 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它對大腦的其他部分發出訊號 , 藉由發電的脈衝信號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	因此 , 我們可以將神經元的發射速率作為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄很多不同的神經元觀察到當動物移動到不同位置時不同的神經會發射信號像這邊這個方形的方形盒子
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起為大腦繪出一張地圖 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在自己的環境中了哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也會被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以 , 癲癇患者有時需要他們監控的腦部電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲他們開車在一個小鎮上開車
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體內的位置細胞就會被活化 , 每當它們開車經過某個特定位置時 , 就會開始發射電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 位置細胞怎麼知道它的環境中老鼠或人類的哪個位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的邊界是特別重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方那張圖標示出老鼠在兩面牆之間的火花 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你把盒子放大 , 發射地點就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面這張圖是當南方靠近一面牆時會被激發出來 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子中放置另一面牆 , 細胞在兩處都會被激發 , 只要在盒子中四處都有一面牆 , 細胞就會被激發 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這個預測是在探測你周圍的界限範圍等等 , 對海馬體是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在對海馬體的輸入資料中 , 針對海馬體的細胞 , 針對特定的邊界或邊緣 , 在探索的過程中 , 發現哪些邊界或老鼠會做出反應 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	你可以發現 , 左邊的細胞當動物靠近東邊的牆的時候 , 就會被激發 , 不論是方形的或是圓形的空間 , 或是在桌子的邊緣讓動物跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞當碰到南方邊界時就會被激發不管是桌面或牆邊的邊緣 , 或甚至是兩張桌子間的隔閡
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 我們認為位置細胞會決定動物在四處探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體的存在 , 例如這個簡單的環境旗幟 , 或者車子的位置 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 看看他們要記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常它們很會把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子在哪裡 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們在位置細胞上做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	這樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟位置的改變是如何改變外在環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你所看到的旗幟是在一個小正方形的環境裡交叉的地方 , 如果你問人們這是在哪裡 , 但是你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟被拉長的方向 , 跟位置細胞被激發的地方完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就好像你會記住旗幟被激發的位置 , 把你所有位置的位置細胞的模式存起來 , 然後你就可以藉由四處走動來找到那個位置 , 所以你最好把你位置細胞被激發的模式和那個位置細胞的模式做匹配 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這會引導你回到你想要記住的地方 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們移動的方向 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們採取一些外出的路徑 , 也許我們停車 , 我們就會知道因為我們自己的動作 , 可以整合這條路的路徑 , 可以追溯回的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從所謂的網格細胞中得到這種途徑整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞又是海馬體輸入訊息 , 有點類似位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每一根細胞就會發射出一系列不同的區域 , 位於整個環境中 , 呈現出驚人的三角形網格 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你記錄一些格狀細胞 , 這裡顯示的不同顏色的格狀 , 每個格子的激發模式在整個環境中 , 都有類似的格狀模式 , 而每個格子的激發模式則相對於其他細胞 , 稍微移轉 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個網格上發射 , 綠色的會發射 , 藍色的在這個上面 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	綜合起來 , 老鼠就可以在其環境中發射位置的虛擬網格有點像是地圖上找到的緯度和經度路線 , 只是用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電訊的活動可以從這些細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 以追蹤它所在的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的動作去知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	正因為這些網格狀細胞激發的對稱性有相同的對稱軸也就是橘色標記的相同方向性表示所有網格的運作會根據位置在六個方向之間的移動而有所改變
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以讓受測者進行核磁共振掃描 , 讓他們玩個小遊戲 , 就像我剛給你們看的這款遊戲 , 來尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	確實 , 你在人腦內看到的是腦內類似的網格細胞 , 其實就是老鼠的網格細胞 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能在想他的車子在哪裡 , 位於距離和方向 , 來延伸建築物和邊界 , 在他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這代表著邊界偵測細胞的激發 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從公園裡走出的這條路 , 會用電網格細胞激發它 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以使位置細胞被激發 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	讓他可以藉由移動找到目前位置的位置來找到目前位置與停車位置位置細胞的發射模式做比對的位置
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那就引導他回到那個位置 , 不考慮視覺暗示他的車子是否真的在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能已經被告知了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡取得它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們觀察整個大腦內的網格狀激發模式 , 我們還會看到它 , 一系列的地點都是在我們進行各種自傳記憶任務時 , 像是當我們最後一次去婚禮 , 舉個例子 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 神經機制能呈現我們周圍的環境 , 也能產生影像 , 這麼一來 , 我們就能重新創造空間景象 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像那些事件時 , 那些事件發生在我們身上的 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這事發生了 , 你的記憶可以藉由位置細胞互相激活 , 通過密集的交互作用再重新啟動邊界細胞 , 創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種我還沒提到的細胞頭部方向細胞 , 它們就像是根據你面對面的哪個方向而發出的指南針 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以從這個方向定義出你想要為你的視覺影像的方向 , 例如 , 你可以想像在這個婚禮上會發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個例子--在認知神經科學裡的新紀元 , 我們開始了解到心理過程 , 像是你怎麼記得、怎麼想 , 甚至是從數十億個獨立神經元所產生的行為來看 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 一個由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾合作推動的全球安全造成的全球安全 , 這不只是開放式粉絲的遠期希望 , 還有北大西洋公約組織 「 詹姆斯•斯特里迪斯 」 , 北大西洋的高層指揮官 , 他們在近期的軍事史上 , 來解釋為何未來應該要建造橋樑而非牆 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、資源、和平、政治、社會媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史特瑞迪:北約的最高指揮官是如何看待全球安全的 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我會提到一些開放資源的安全性 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須在安全上有更好的表現 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先讓我們回顧一下20世紀安全這個概念對我們來說是如何運作的
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人死亡 , 約兩千人一天 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它推向第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到斯大林格戰 , 300天 , 2千萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝 , 到二戰的馬其頓防線 , 然後進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的主題是 , 不要建造城牆來建立安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲一座知名的橋樑
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	橋樑接近dina河流 , 由irvoandrice所創作的小說主題 , 它談到在歐洲和巴爾幹半島這一帶有巨大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫著要融合在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我想再次強調 , 開放資源的安全性是把國際的 , 跨部門的 , 私人的公共的 , 用策略性的溝通 , 主要是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們全球的公有物受到攻擊 , 採用各種形式的攻擊 , 沒有針對全球公有物的威脅可以用建設圍牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 線從輪廓穿過印度洋
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	音樂會在音樂會的一邊有鋼琴鋼索 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	這可以預防海盜來攻擊海盜 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜現在全世界是一種非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也在馬拉加的海峽非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在幾內亞灣很活躍 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是全球交通運輸體系中一個10億美元的不連續性的損失 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名船員被綁架 ,
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何解決這個問題 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	咱們轉變到另一種海洋 , 網路的海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	此時此刻 , 他們被監禁 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 淨利超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 全球經濟年額二十兆美元的不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年有兩萬億 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這僅僅是英國的國內生產毛額 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這種網絡世界 , 我們無止盡地知道它是最根本的開放 , 在威脅下也一樣是如此 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我在全球公有物中擔憂的另一件事 , 就是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 由鴉片類藥物的運動所造成 , 由阿富汗穿過歐洲 , 到達美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從andeanridge北部來的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運輸 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	大部分的人口販賣活動在海洋上 , 但在全球的其他公有物上也一樣 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位 , 這是美國海軍太空總署用來阻止人口販運的高科技產品 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個販毒集團的半潛水的實驗 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美的叢林裡建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用低科技的木筏逮捕了它 , 裝載了六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個船員 , 精良的溝通掃描 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種運送麻醉劑 , 人體 , 武器 , 上帝禁止 , 大規模殺傷性武器是對全球公有物的威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們集結在今天的阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一塊地 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	全世界80%到90%的小狗鴉片和海洛因來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到了恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是基地組織建立的地方 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的暴動就在那兒 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以這種恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須處理的是什麼 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 在21世紀 ,
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道二十世紀的工具是行不通的 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不會僅僅依靠槍支來遞送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不能僅僅依靠槍支 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須表現的很好而且很有競爭力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際的 , 跨部門的 , 私人和公共的聯繫 , 通過互聯網溝通而引導 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這是如何用正面的方式運作的 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗的士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 , 我想我曾讀到過這個人口統計數字在二十多歲和三十多歲的年輕人在阿富汗大都不識字 。 」
you would be correct .	你可能會是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	進入安全部隊之後 , 85%無法閱讀 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為在這些男人和女人學會閱讀的時期 , 塔利班的沉迷教育 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們教導他們閱讀 , 通過北約和私人機構的互動課程 , 和發展機構的合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教了超過20萬的阿富汗安全部隊 , 基本的讀和寫 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你在阿富汗讀和寫的時候 , 通常你可以把筆放進口袋 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在畢業典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們很驕傲的拿起筆 , 放在他們的口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	全球有50個國家參與了這項任務這些發展機構和公共的私人和公共的開發機構來對付這種安全
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	我們當然也教他們格鬥技巧 , 但我認為 , 開放式安全意味著為創造更持久的安全 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	叫做 「 安慰 」 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘姐妹船叫做默西 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	安慰號在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人的治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在一般的巡迴演出中 , 他們會進行四十萬個治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	船員不是嚴格的執勤者 , 而是結合人道主義組織:營運希望、微笑專案 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織送來志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	內部的醫生出來了 。
they're all part of this .	這些都是其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子來說 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 和他的媽媽走了兩天來到安慰號上的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被配備時 , 經過他那非常不可思議的目光 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界了 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	把這個乘以四十萬名病人治療 , 這個私人和保安部隊合作 , 你就會開始發現 , 用一種非常不同的方式來創造安全 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你可以從這張照片中挑出兩名美國陸軍士兵嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們可能是這兩名年輕男子這可能是棒球診所的一部分我們探討了國務院大聯盟不同部門的合作他們設立了軍事棒球隊的球員他們是真正的軍人他們是有技能的軍人他們會在拉丁美洲和加勒比地區開了診所他們會在荷蘭開設立美洲和加勒比地區開設在保加勒斯坦共和加勒斯共和加勒比州開設在全美洲
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它向年輕人展示了關於健身 , 和生活的榜樣 , 我認為幫助我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這種合作的另一面是在災後救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍的直升機 , 在2004年 , 海嘯導致25 , 000人死亡 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些重大的災難中2004年海嘯 , 250000死 , 2005年巴基斯坦的kashmiri大地震 , 8萬5千死亡 , 海地地震 , 30萬人的死亡 , 更近代的地震雙重組日本和其核能產業在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到國際間 , 跨部門之間的合作 , 和公私之間的合作 , 與自然力量一起合作 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些是關於 「 開放式安全 」 這個概念的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們用這種方式將它綁在一起 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你看著這個想法: 「 啊 , 米德 , 這些一定是溝通的海道 , 或者這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是推特的圖表
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特的 。 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	這能喚起全世界六大人口調查的興起:中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特 , 和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要進入這些蚊帳呢 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談過阿拉伯之春 , 以及它的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉一個例子 , 就是你如何傳遞訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦演講過一陣子 , 說到這裡 , 我對你們說 , 我在facebook上 。 朋友是我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾有點笑 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	那時有一篇文章 , 由ap發表在電線上 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	世界上有兩個地方 , 芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:北約艦隊司令需要好友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是個催化劑 , 隔天早上我有上百個facebook好友請求 , 來自印尼和芬蘭 , 他們通常會說: 「 司令 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 娜托是什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們大笑 , 但這是我們如何移動訊息 , 移動那個訊息就是我們連結國際、國際、私人和社交網絡的方法 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我說個嚴肅的話 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一位勇敢的英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛隊 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他正站在赫爾曼南部 , 阿富汗南部 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我把他放出來是想提醒我們 , 我不希望有人離開這間房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、有能力的軍事力量 , 就可以創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	那就是我們是誰的核心 , 我們做的是保護自由 , 言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍視的事物 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道 , 人生並不是個開端的轉換 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要軍隊在戰鬥中 , 或在兵營中 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會主張生活是萬能動搖的 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須把安全感放進去 。 正如我所想的 , 在21世紀 , 我們會把真正的戰爭和危機 , 運用在真正的戰爭和危機中 , 但將會有很多次的例子 , 就像我們今天所說的 , 我們的軍隊可以是創造21世紀安全、國際 , 跨部門 , 私人和公共事務的一部分 , 透過溝通來連結 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我想說今天早些時候聽到的關於維基百科的消息 。 我經常使用維基百科檢視事實 , 就像你們都知道的 , 維基百科不是由12個聰明的人鎖在房間裡寫文章 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	每天 , 維基百科是數萬人輸入信息 , 每一天 , 就有數百萬人提取信息 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這完美的形象是沒有一個人能這麼聰明 , 能讓我們一起思考 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個我們一起想的那麼聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的宣言很簡單:這個世界 , 所有人類都可以自由地分享所有知識 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 通過結合國際 , 跨部門 , 私人 , 戰略溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們能創造出安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。
